Japanese Night Flight Accident

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Communications began operating nighttime air mail service on November 1st, and the results have been very good for half a month. However, due to inadequate nighttime equipment, at 7:20 last night, its aircraft collided with a tall building and crashed, destroying the fuselage and injuring the pilot. Nighttime aviation training is of great importance for air defense during wartime. The Japanese Ministry of Military and Ministry of Communications have decided to strictly investigate the cause of the accident to provide a reference for nighttime aviation equipment. (China United Press dispatch, 24th)

President Murayama of Asahi Shimbun Passes Away

(Osaka) Murayama Ryuhei, the president of the Osaka Asahi Shimbun and Tokyo Asahi Shimbun, and a member of the House of Peers, previously suffered from a cold and was recuperating. Recently, pneumonia developed as a complication, and his condition deteriorated, passing away at his home in the countryside this morning at 3:00 AM, at the age of 84. Mr. Murayama was a famous scholar of national learning, born in Mie Prefecture, the eldest son of Murayama Morio. In the fourth year of Meiji (1871), he went to Osaka to run a Western goods store. From the fourteenth year of Meiji (1881), he accepted the publication of a tri-weekly newspaper by Kimura Heihachi. Thereafter, he engaged in the newspaper business, which was the predecessor of the Osaka Asahi Shimbun. In recent years, he fought fiercely and consolidated the foundation of the newspaper. In the twenty-second year of Meiji (1889), he bought the Tokyo Mezamashi Shimbun, renamed it the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun, and worked hard to struggle. The east and west echoed each other, leading to today's greatness. In the fourth year of Taisho (1915), he was awarded the Third Class Order of Merit for his achievements and awarded the Order of the Sacred Treasure. He was elected twice as a member of the House of Representatives and is currently a member of the House of Peers. His wife, Masuko, had no children and adopted Murayama Nagake, a director of the company, as her adopted son. (Dentsu dispatch, 24th)

The Sarraut Cabinet in France Falls Before Completing a Month in Office; Finance Bill Fails Again in Parliament; President Extends Interviews to Party Leaders to Discuss Cabinet Formation

(Paris) The government's financial austerity bill was discussed clause by clause in the Chamber of Deputies today. As a result, the government's proposal failed to obtain the Chamber's agreement, and the Sarraut Cabinet resigned. The previous Daladier Cabinet was overthrown on the night of the 23rd of last month due to the rejection of the financial bill. The Sarraut Cabinet was formed on the 27th, less than a month ago. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) A motion by the right-wing parties to reduce salaries in the finance bill was approved by 326 votes, with 427 against. This motion failed. The Socialist Party then proposed an amendment to exempt salaries. Sarraut spoke out against it, and Herriot followed up with a speech supporting the government. However, the vote resulted in 427 votes in favor and 321 votes against. The government took this as a vote of confidence, leading to the cabinet's collapse. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Cabinet formation consultations began this morning. At 9:30 AM, President Lebrun met with Senate President Jeanneney. After meeting with the President, Jeanneney declared, "I believe that this kind of cabinet turmoil must stop. This is a critical time concerning the fate of France, which is more important than all partisan disputes." Furthermore, Jacques, the general rapporteur of the Chamber of Deputies' Finance Committee, declared after meeting with the President that it has never been easier than yesterday to find a majority to pass the financial adjustment bill. According to his observations, yesterday there were indeed a majority of members who supported tax revenue and the reform of the financial oversight administrative organs, as well as the temporary taxation of salaries. The President is scheduled to continue consultations at 2:30 PM. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

A Small Victory Before the Failure

(Paris) The French Sarraut Cabinet was only recently established, but this morning it won a small victory on the finance bill in the Chamber of Deputies before suffering defeat, ultimately leading to its resignation.

Sudden Change in Atmosphere Within Two Hours

The fall of the Sarraut Cabinet was extremely abrupt. At around midnight, the parliament had given a vote of confidence of 326 to 237 on the government's proposed amendment to the budget, after a heated debate on the general reduction of salaries for civil and military officials. However, in less than two hours, a new motion from the Socialist Party, led by Gounin, to amend Clause 6 – opposing the exemption from income tax for civil servants whose annual salaries are less than 10,000 francs – gained a vote of no confidence with 321 votes against 247. Sarraut immediately retreated into a side room with his cabinet members. After a brief consultation, they announced their resignation and submitted their resignations to President Lebrun, who announced the acceptance of the cabinet's resignation at 3 AM this morning.

Complex Elements Voting in Opposition

It is reported that the initial vote of confidence was due to the efforts of former Finance Minister Flandin, the leader of the Republican Left. Flandin had rallied most of the centrist and center-left members to support the government, and the Radical Socialist Party, led by former Prime Minister Herriot, also fully supported the government. The vote of no confidence two hours later was due to the united opposition of the right-wing Central Party and the new Socialist Party. Therefore, the number of votes in favor of the government the first time and the number of votes against the government the second time were similar. (National News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) Last night's vote in the Chamber of Deputies, which overthrew the Sarraut Cabinet, was made up of members from various parties and factions within the Chamber, including members from the Communist Party, the Socialist Party, the New Socialist Party, the Central Party, and the right-wing parties.

No Way to See Political Tendencies

Therefore, last night's vote did not indicate a definite political tendency. Since the beginning of this parliament, the introduction of the financial adjustment bill has caused three waves of cabinet changes. It is difficult to discern from last night's vote which path the solution to this cabinet change should lean towards. Therefore, it is too early to speculate on the person who will be commissioned to form a new cabinet. This will only be known after the customary cabinet formation consultations have taken place. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

Doumergue to Form a Cabinet of National Unity?

(Paris) According to well-informed sources, the successor is likely to be Doumergue, who will contact the Central Party to organize a cabinet of national unity. It is feared that cabinet members will be largely changed, except that Poincaré will likely continue as Minister of Finance and Daladier will likely continue as Minister of the Army. (National News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) The current difficult problem is the choice of a successor. Doumergue, Herriot, and Daladier have all served as Prime Ministers. There is currently talk of them succeeding in forming a cabinet. The Sarraut government was only established for a month, and was unable to maintain its position for long due to the attacks of the Socialist Party. According to the views of observers, Doumergue may be able to form a mixed government of left-wing parties, but it is unlikely to last long. However, it may open the way for Herriot or Daladier to organize a centralized government. Only this kind of centralized government can have sufficient authority to obtain the necessary votes for a balanced budget bill. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

Germany Promulgates New Press Law; Violators Face Death or Imprisonment

(Berlin) The new law terminating freedom of speech for newspapers was published today. It stipulates that journalists who violate the law will face punishments such as being blacklisted, fined, or imprisoned, depending on the nature of the crime. Part of the press law was previously implemented by cabinet order, stipulating that words that instill treason must be punished with the death penalty or 15 years of imprisonment. According to the new law, journalists must not publish in newspapers (1) words that mix personal interests with public interests to confuse the public; (2) news that undermines the power of the German government at home and abroad; (3) words that weaken the unified will of the German people; (4) words that weaken national preparedness; (5) words that are sufficient to damage German cultural and economic life and religious sentiments, and words that damage the reputation and dignity of others with slanderous and mocking tones. (National News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Previously, Belgian professor Piccard reached an altitude of 53,530 feet, and a Soviet balloon had reached over 59,000 feet. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

(Washington) Litvinov telegraphed aeronauts Settle and Fordney, who flew into the stratosphere, congratulating them on their success and hoping that the cooperation between the Soviet Union and the United States in science and engineering would lead to greater achievements. (Tianjin) Since the Incident in Tangshan, the number of Japanese and Koreans has been increasing daily, operating drug businesses and often causing disturbances, resulting in repeated fatal cases. Jin Shuren Case Opens Preliminary Hearing; Complex Circumstances Mean Official Prosecution is Still Distant

(Nanjing) In the Jin Shuren case, Chief Prosecutor Sun Wei of the District Court opened the first preliminary hearing on the morning of the 24th. Those summoned for questioning included Ai Sha, Fan Maoru, Mu Weixin, Shali Han, and Mu Tianmin. The defendant Jin Shuren was present in court. The prosecutor asked Jin about each of the charges against him and allowed him to present factual defenses. As this was a preliminary hearing, public attendance was prohibited. The head of the court said that the circumstances of this case were complex and the investigation procedures were extremely cumbersome. At least three to five hearings would be required to gain a considerable understanding, and the date for official prosecution would be next year. (Special dispatch, 24th)

Legislative Yuan Passes the Regulations for Awarding Medals and Revises the Law on the Discipline of Public Officials

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan convened its 40th meeting of the 3rd session at 9 a.m. on the 24th, with 64 attendees including Wang Qi. Sun Ke presided, and Liang Hancao served as Secretary-General. Matters discussed: (1) Review of the draft amendment to the Special Industries Encouragement Law, resolved to be referred to the Economics Committee in conjunction with the Legal System Committee for review. (2) Review of the draft amendment to Articles 1 and 8 of the Administrative Litigation Law, resolved to be referred to the Legal System Committee for review. (3) The report of the Commerce Law Committee of this Yuan on the review and amendment of Article 129 of the Company Law was resolved to be passed according to the review report. (4) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan on the review of the draft Regulations for Awarding Medals was resolved to be amended and passed. (5) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan on the review and amendment of Article 3 of the Law on the Discipline of Public Officials was resolved to be passed. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan discussed the Regulations for Awarding Medals at its plenary session on the 24th, which were amended and passed. The case was referred by the Central Political Council with attached principles, stating that these regulations are for awarding medals to heads of friendly nations, their people, and our country's envoys abroad, to meet diplomatic needs. During this time of national crisis, all other awarding matters will be suspended. The Legislative Yuan intends to state this intention in a document submitted to the National Government, so that an explanation can be included when it is promulgated in the future. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) The original text of the Regulations for Awarding Medals passed by the Legislative Yuan at its 40th meeting on the 24th: Article 1: Any citizen of the Republic of China who has rendered meritorious service to the nation or society, excluding active-duty military personnel who shall be handled in accordance with the Regulations for Medals of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, may be awarded medals by the National Government. The National Government, for the purpose of fostering friendly relations, may specially award medals to heads of friendly nations or bestow them upon the people of friendly nations. Article 2: Medals are divided into the following two types: (1) Order of the Jadeite; (2) Jadeite Medal. Article 3: The Order of the Jadeite, in addition to being worn by the Chairman of the National Government, may be specially awarded by the National Government to heads of friendly nations. Article 4: The Jadeite Medal is divided into nine classes. Public officials who are elected or specially appointed are initially awarded the third class; those who are recommended for appointment are initially awarded the fifth class; those who are nominated for appointment are initially awarded the seventh class; and those who are commissioned for appointment are initially awarded the ninth class. All may gradually advance to the first class through accumulated merit. Medals awarded to non-public officials are initially awarded the ninth class and may gradually advance to the first class through accumulated merit. Article 5: The awarding of medals to public officials of friendly nations shall be handled with reference to the official rank of each country and the provisions of paragraph 1 of the preceding article. Non-public officials shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 2 of the preceding article. Article 6: The awarding of medals shall be in accordance with the provisions of the preceding two articles and shall not exceed the initial awarding rank, except when specially ordered by the Chairman of the National Government. Article 7: The design, ribbon system, color distinction of the medals, and the color distinction of the accompanying medal ribbon and ribbon color shall be determined by the National Government. Article 8: The awarding of medals to elected and specially appointed public officials shall be carried out by order of the National Government. Public officials below the rank of recommended appointment shall have the facts of their meritorious service and resumes submitted by the competent authority to the superior authority, forwarded to the Ministry of Personnel for review, and then submitted to the Examination Yuan to request the National Government to award the medals. The awarding of medals to non-public officials shall be reviewed and submitted by the Ministry of Interior. The awarding of medals to the people of friendly nations shall be reviewed and submitted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Article 9: Matters concerning the filling out and registration of medal certificates shall be handled by the Ministry of Personnel for public officials, by the Ministry of Interior for non-public officials, and by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for the people of friendly nations. Article 10: The awarding of medals shall be carried out on National Day, except when specially ordered by the Chairman of the National Government. When elected and specially appointed public officials are awarded medals, the Chairman of the National Government shall personally award them. If the recipient is unable to receive the medal in person due to special circumstances, the National Government may send personnel to award it on their behalf. The remainder shall be awarded by the competent head or the head of the original submitting authority. When the Chairman of the National Government specially awards the Order of the Jadeite to the heads of friendly nations, a special envoy or the ambassador to the country shall be sent to present it. The procedures for awarding medals to the people of friendly nations shall be determined by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Article 11: When promoted to receive a medal, all those except elected and specially appointed public officials shall return the previously received medal to the local administrative office or embassy or consulate, which shall forward it to the Ministry of Personnel, the Ministry of Interior, or the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for submission to the National Government for cancellation, but the medal certificate need not be returned. Article 12: All those who have received medals may enjoy them for life, but those who have been sentenced to deprivation of public rights due to a crime shall return the medal and medal certificate together in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1 of the preceding article. Article 13: The detailed rules for the implementation of these regulations and the ceremony for receiving medals shall be jointly determined by the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry of Personnel. Article 14: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) The original text of Article 3, paragraph 2 of the amended Law on the Discipline of Public Officials passed by the Legislative Yuan: Article 3, paragraph 2: The punishments in items 2 to 4 of the preceding paragraph shall not apply to elected political officials, members of the Legislative Yuan, and members of the Control Yuan. The punishment in item 2 shall not apply to specially appointed political officials. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

After consultation with the six ministries, the proposed relief measures are: (1) reducing freight rates for domestic goods to reduce their costs; (2) levying anti-dumping duties on foreign goods to protect domestic goods from foreign competition. After the Assassination of Qiu Yuanwu, the Court Examined the Corpse and Found a Total of Seven Wounds; Military and Political Authorities Strictly Limit the Arrest of the Mastermind

(Xi'an) After Qiu Yuanwu was attacked and killed by reactionary elements on the evening of the 21st, the body was moved to the Xijing Daily that night. The colleagues of the newspaper immediately formed the Qiu Yuanwu Funeral Committee to handle the funeral. All newspaper affairs are the responsibility of the colleagues and will continue as usual without any slackening. The local court sent personnel to examine the body at noon on the 22nd. There were seven wounds on the whole body: one knife wound on the top of the left skull, one wound on the back of the neck, one gunshot wound entry on the left shoulder, one gunshot wound exit on the lower left chest, one stab wound on the right middle abdomen, with the mesentery protruding, one stab wound on the upper left arm, and one stab wound on the left wrist. The face was blurred and covered in blood. All the guests and colleagues of the newspaper present could not help but weep. Mrs. Qiu, holding her five-year-old eldest son and three-year-old young child, wailed on the ground and fainted on the spot. The scene was too tragic to bear. The body was placed in a coffin at 12 p.m. without closing the lid, waiting for the central government to send personnel to examine it before closing the lid. In recent days, important party and state figures have sent telegrams of condolence and sympathy to the family. Leaders of various party, government, and military agencies and the press also sent condolences. Director Yang was extremely furious about this case and ordered his subordinates to arrest the murderer within a limited time. Chairman Shao has telegraphed Acting Chairman Hu, limiting the investigation to be solved within four days. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

Chiang Kai-shek's Special Commissioner Stationed in Sichuan to Supervise the Suppression of Bandits; Xu's Bandits Flee to the Border of Shaanxi, Yang's Troops Ordered to Intercept; He's Bandits in Eastern Sichuan in Contact with Liu Xiang's Troops

Hankou Correspondence: Xu Xiangqian's bandit troops have recently been rampaging in Sichuan Province, advancing on three fronts. One group is in contact with Tian Songyao's army along the Zhaoguang-Cangbao line, attempting to cross the Jialing River to occupy the strategic Jianmen Pass. Another group is confronting Liu Xiang's army along the Sui-Xuan-Kaijiang line, waiting for an opportunity to advance eastward to meet He Long. A third group is heading north out of Chengkou to spy on southern Shaanxi, seeking to open the road between Sichuan and Shaanxi. Apart from the Jialing River battle, the truth of which is unknown due to inconvenient transportation and the need for several days for written messages to reach Hankou, the eastern Sichuan army, Wang Lingji and Fan Shaozeng's troops, have now crossed the Qu River and occupied Sanhui. Yang Sen's troops are also attacking Zhoukou, indicating that Suiding and Yingshan have not yet been completely recovered, and the distance to Xuanhan is even greater. On the northern front, the bandits first occupied Chengkou and continued to advance north. It is heard that they have reached Zhenba in southern Shaanxi. It is unpredictable where they will develop in the future. The central government has long been prepared for the bandits' northward flight. Yang Hucheng's troops have been ordered to station in Hanzhong and contact Feng Qincheng and other troops to strictly intercept them. Chiang Kai-shek, because the Sichuan armies were mostly waiting and watching, fearing that they would miss the military opportunity, telegraphed Liu Xiang, transferring the order to the armies to join forces to suppress the bandits. Yesterday, he telegraphed Liu again, reiterating the previous order, and said that if they continued to wait and watch and not advance, they would be dealt with by military law. Yang Deyuan, Chen Xingya, Yu Kedong, Wang Xiangting, Lei Biao, Li Anzhi, and Li Leifu were appointed as special commissioners to supervise the suppression of bandits in Sichuan, and Yang and others have already taken a ship west from Hankou on the 22nd. Now Chiang has also appointed Cheng Zerun as the special military commissioner stationed in Sichuan, stationed permanently in Sichuan, responsible for supervising the suppression of bandits, which shows Chiang's attention to the situation in Sichuan. He Long and Xia Xi's remnant bandits have recently been using all their strength to flee to Sichuan. He Long himself is still in Wangjiaying in Lichuan, directing the westward advance. Liu Xiang has sent the 21st Army, Chen's division, to meet them, and they have been in contact with one of the bandit groups in Tanxiangdong in eastern Sichuan. According to reports, the bandits retreated after being attacked, and the division has advanced to Lefudian, pressing on the main force of He's bandits in Jiannan. On the Hubei side, Xu Yuanquan is leading a large army to track and suppress them. After establishing contact with Chen's division, they will agree on a date for a general offensive. (23rd)

He Chengjun Talks About the Fujian Incident, Says It Does Not Affect the Bandit Suppression Military Operations; Provinces Along the Yangtze River Will Request the Punishment of Chen

Hankou Correspondence: He Chengjun went to Jiangxi with Liu Zhenhua on the 15th to visit Chiang, and arrived in Nanchang on the 16th. During the meeting, Chiang gave detailed instructions on bandit suppression, post-war rehabilitation, local administration, and immigration. On the 22nd, He and Liu went to Xun together. On the 23rd, Liu took a ship from Xun to Anqing. He and Peng Zhenshan took the Jianguo ship west and arrived in Hankou at about 9 p.m. According to He, the bandit suppression and the Fujian incident can be summarized as follows: "The Fujian Incident was instigated by a few people. The doctrine they put forward has not gained the sympathy of all parties, and the elements are extremely complicated. Guangdong and Guangxi have expressed their opposition, and the elders have also criticized their fallacies. Mr. Hu Zhantang especially felt heartbroken that they openly abolished the party. It is expected that they will soon perish on their own, and it will have absolutely no impact on the overall situation and the bandit suppression military operations. The central government has decided to resolve this incident with political means, and does not want to lightly start a war. Internal and external troubles, mutually persecuting each other, water and drought successively arriving, people's lives are haggard. Unless absolutely necessary, they do not want to find another way other than peace. Chairman Chiang has always maintained calmness and ordered the generals of the Sichuan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Henan provinces to continue their efforts to complete the work of bandit suppression. Now the military in Jiangxi is winning victories, and the battle of Huwan completely defeated the pseudo-15th Army Corps. The bandit leaders Lin Biao and Peng Dehuai only escaped with their lives. More than 1,000 rifles, 100 machine guns, and countless other military supplies were captured, which is a new record of victory since the suppression of bandits. Other provinces have also made progress. Commander-in-Chief Liu Xueya will leave Xun for Anqing today to handle government affairs. After staying for a few days, he will return to his defense via Hankou. The rumors that he will be transferred are absolutely false. I will leave for the eastern and western Hubei provinces within days to inspect the bandit suppression situation and post-war progress. The return date to Hankou cannot be predetermined." That evening, Cao Haosen, Xia Douyin, Wan Yaohuang, Zhang Zhenhan, Shen Ke, and others went to He's private residence one after another to inquire about the Fujian incident. It is said that the seven provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang will jointly telegraph the central government, ordering the open punishment of Chen Mingshu and others. (23rd)

Two New Plans of the Jiangsu Provincial Government: Organizing a Opium Prohibition Committee; Increasing the Authority of Various Commissioners

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Jiangsu Provincial Government has properly planned for matters concerning opium prohibition and the authority of supervising commissioners. The following is a brief description:

Eradicating Opium Addiction Throughout the Province After Chairman Chen took office, he believed that opium prohibition in the province had been lax in the past, and there were many malpractices. He now plans to organize a Opium Prohibition Committee in the provincial capital, and plans to establish branches in various counties. It is heard that the province will appoint the provincial government committee members as ex officio members, and add several leaders of French legal entities and local gentry in the provincial capital to participate. In addition to the county magistrate and public security bureau chief (or the section chief if the bureau is abolished) as ex officio members in various counties, several local legal entity leaders and gentry will also be added to participate. Each association will also set up an opium rehabilitation hospital. Those found to be smoking opium will first be sent to the hospital for rehabilitation, and then given appropriate punishment. It is also heard that Chairman Chen advocates for the sake of quick results, and plans to shorten the six-year prohibition period to four years, so as to eliminate opium addiction throughout the province within these four years, so that there will not be a single opium addict in the entire Jiangsu.

Increasing the Authority of Commissioners The province's supervising commissioners are divided into thirteen districts, and the county magistrate where the commissioner's office is located concurrently serves as the commissioner. After Chairman Chen took office, he believed that the commissioner system was very complete, but too many districts made the efficiency scattered, making it difficult to concentrate power. Moreover, once the commissioner concurrently serves as the county magistrate where the district is located, it is inevitable that obstruction will occur when supervising and directing other county magistrates. It is now heard that the number of supervising offices in the province will be reduced from thirteen districts to nine districts, and it is advocated that the commissioners should not concurrently serve as county magistrates. It is also planned to expand the authority and responsibilities of the commissioners. The commissioner's work location is not limited to being stationed in a certain county all the time, and it is also planned to set up a station in each county under its jurisdiction, so that each commissioner can move around and carefully observe all political affairs. The meaning is no different from the patrol road of the Qing Dynasty. The commissioners will also conduct a monthly inspection. If there is any corruption or improper handling by the county magistrates, they will be given guidance or punishment at any time. It is heard that Minister of Civil Affairs Gu also strongly agreed that the commissioner system must have the above-mentioned changes. Once all the committee members fully agree, it is expected that it can be implemented in January 1934.

Change of District Head in Songjiang's First District

Zhong Taichi, the district head of Songjiang's first district, has been in office for four years. Recently, rumors circulated that District Head Zhong had financial improprieties and embezzlements. Half a month ago, County Magistrate Jin summoned District Head Zhong for questioning about the facts. Immediately after, he requested the province to remove Zhong Taichi from his position and recommended Li Zufú and Dù Guī for approval. At 11 PM on the 23rd, the county government received an order from the province approving the removal of District Head Zhong and the appointment of Li Zufu to fill the vacancy. Yesterday morning, the new District Head Li received instructions from the county magistrate, requiring him to complete the handover by the morning of the 24th. District Head Zhong, citing insufficient time for preparation, negotiated a one-day extension. Consequently, it was decided that the handover would take place this morning.

Filial Daughter in Wuxi Punished for Thinking of Her Mother

Zhang, a woman from the back alley of Dongbeitang in the Sixth District, is 72 years old. Her daughter is married to Wang Qinren from Ao Qingpu. Wang used to be a section chief in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs during the Beijing government era and is currently managing donations in Beiping, earning a considerable income. Therefore, Zhang Wang has been living with her son-in-law and beloved daughter in Beiping. In May of this year, Wang's stomach illness recurred, and due to her advanced age and the inconvenience of living away from home, she returned to her hometown to recuperate. After three months of illness, she recently recovered. Her daughter in Beiping, missing her elderly mother and concerned about her recent recovery and the need for care, purchased two boxes of ginseng in Beiping. Considering that opium could also treat her mother's stomach illness, she specially prepared twelve opium pills, packed them inside the ginseng boxes, and sent them via express mail to Wuxi. The mailed package arrived in Wuxi the day before yesterday. Zhang Wang asked her neighbor, Peng Xinhè, to collect it from the post office without informing him of the package's contents. When Peng arrived at the post office, the staff, following protocol, asked what the package contained. Peng, taken aback and unaware, could not answer, raising suspicion. The post office then telegraphed the county court, which dispatched a prosecutor, a clerk, and bailiffs to the post office to jointly open and inspect the package. They discovered twelve opium pills and immediately took the witness to the court for interrogation. The court ordered Peng Xinhè to post bail and demanded that he bring Zhang Wang to court. Yesterday, Peng accompanied Zhang Wang to the court. The prosecutor interrogated them again, resulting in Peng Xinhè being dismissed, Zhang Wang being released on bail, the twelve opium pills being confiscated, and the two boxes of ginseng being returned to her.

Bandit Executed in Hangzhou's Gudang

Yuan Jintao, a resident near the Caishen Temple in Gudang, Hangzhou, was suddenly kidnapped by four bandits at around 6 PM on the 21st of this month. The bandits abducted Yuan and fled. After the incident was reported, the local defense corps, together with the military police, pursued the bandits and captured one, Yuan Jinshao, in Taoyuanling. The hostage took the opportunity to escape and return home. The captured bandit was taken to the security office for interrogation and confessed without hesitation. Yesterday (the 24th) at 4 PM, he was escorted to the scene of the crime in Gudang and executed by firing squad.

Six Members of a Family Kidnapped Simultaneously in Jiaxing

The town of Youchegang in this county is separated by a river from the town of Tianningzhuang in Jiashan. Recently, Tianningzhuang has been raising funds in the name of a public entertainment park, staging performances day and night. Dozens of residents from Youchegang are attracted to it day and night. The day before yesterday, a Mr. Shan, a visitor from Shaoxing, returned home late at night after watching a play. His entire family of six was kidnapped by bandits. Although three have been released, the whereabouts of the remaining three are still unknown. Chen Jingxian, the mayor of Chengxi (Youchegang), recognizing the seriousness of the situation, has telegraphed the provincial government, the Security Office, and the Department of Civil Affairs, urging the Jiashan County Government to immediately close the theater in Tianningzhen to eliminate hidden dangers.

Fire at Yancang Bridge in Shaoxing

A fire broke out in the Yancang Bridge area inside the Xiguo Gate of Shaoxing at around 6 PM on the 22nd. The fire originated in the Shan family's residence in Tangjiatai. Due to the prolonged lack of rain and extreme dryness, the fire spread to five or six neighboring houses, including those of Yu Yiran and others. With the arrival of firefighters from various locations, efforts were made to extinguish the fire. After two hours, the fire was finally put out. An estimated fifty to sixty houses were destroyed.

Gambling Den Cracked Down in Lvsi, Nantong

County Magistrate Cheng Yuyan and Provincial Committee Member Xu Youchuan went to inspect the rural areas and learned that there was a large gambling den in Lvsi, protected by the Public Security Bureau, operating openly with significant winnings and losses. They immediately dispatched a police team to surround and arrest the gamblers, capturing one thousand offenders and gambling paraphernalia. The owner, Sister Jiang Da, was sentenced to thirty days of detention, and the others were punished accordingly. Peng Tiesheng, the director of the Lvsi Public Security Bureau, was immediately dismissed from his post.

Tragic News After the Kidnapping of Zhou Chengfang in Gaoyou

Zhou Chengfang, a farmer from Sangshutou in the fourth district of this county, was kidnapped by dozens of bandits and taken to the Zhangjiaxia area of the district several days ago. The bandits repeatedly threatened his family, demanding a ransom of five thousand yuan. The family agreed to pay three thousand yuan, but the bandits refused. The day before yesterday, the bandits cruelly cut off Zhou's ears and sent him home, instructing his family to quickly prepare five thousand yuan for his ransom, or they would kill him. After speaking, they took Zhou away again.

Yizheng Police Captain in Yangzhou Charged and Detained

Shi Yujin, a resident of the northern part of Yizheng County, has been running a grain store for years. He was previously accused of being a bandit and smoking opium at the county police headquarters. The police captain, Chen Guoan, led the police to arrest Shi and then released him. After being released, Shi accused Captain Chen Guoan of soliciting a bribe of one thousand yuan during his detention, which constituted dereliction of duty and fraud. He filed a complaint with the High Court. After approval by the High Court, the Jiangdu Branch Court was designated as the receiving agency. Yesterday, the court session was held. After strict questioning, Shi Yujin was released on bail, and Chen Guoan provided a written guarantee of five hundred yuan. Since Chen had no guarantor, he was detained.

Bandits Discovered in the Fifth District of Qingjiang

The fifth district of Huaiyin County is vast and borders the three counties of Lianmu, Siyang. Bandit robberies occur from time to time. On the 22nd, bandits were discovered between Wulizhuang and Xuliu in the district, intending to cause trouble. Shen Bingchu, the captain of the local police brigade, upon receiving a report, immediately led a squad of mounted police and about a platoon of foot police towards the fifth district at 4 PM that day. He also mobilized various defense squads and security corps along the way to search and defend the area around Wulizhuang and Xuliu.

News from This City: Chu Minyi Discusses the Central Government's Handling of the Fujian Incident, Wang Lunqin Arrives in Shanghai on the Jiangzhen Warship, Feng Yuxiang Has Not Left Mount Tai

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, arrived in Shanghai last night at 11 PM via a night train from Nanjing. He disembarked at the North Station at 7:30 AM this morning and returned to his private residence on Avenue Albert to rest. A Central News Agency reporter visited Mr. Chu this morning and inquired about the central government's measures to deal with the Fujian Incident. He provided a detailed response as follows:

The Significance of the Fujian Incident is Particularly Serious

According to Mr. Chu, the political changes in the past few years have all been internal party disputes. This time, however, it is different. Not only did they betray the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, abolish the Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth flag, but they also colluded with the communists, recognizing the enemy as their father. All of this proves that they have betrayed the party, ruined the people, and attempted to overthrow the country. Therefore, the significance of this incident is more serious than any past party disputes.

Most Heartbreaking: Material Support for the Communists

Jiangxi Province has been blockading the communist areas for many months to cut off the communists' material supplies, in order to be able to eliminate them completely. This time, Fujian's collusion with the communists, providing them with material support, has destroyed months of blockade efforts in one fell swoop. This action not only affects the military's suppression of the communists but is also the most heartbreaking aspect of the Fujian Incident.

Central Government's Separate Handling Methods

The main figures in this Fujian Incident, such as Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, Chen Youren, etc., are all members of the Central Committee. Therefore, the central government first expelled the three from the party and handed them over to the government for strict arrest and punishment. Other party members who followed the rebellion will also be severely punished if they do not wake up. The central government had previously decided not to use force to deal with the Fujian Incident. However, if the Fujian army takes any aggressive actions, the central government will send troops to surround Fujian Province and strictly defend it. Orders have been issued to the military and political authorities to prepare and handle the situation as appropriate.

Central Government Sends Personnel to Hong Kong to Welcome Hu

The central government, recognizing the severity of the national crisis and the occurrence of the Fujian Incident, has decided to convene the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee on December 20 to unite and jointly discuss national salvation plans. It has also decided to send personnel to the south to urge Mr. Hu Zhan Tang and the Southwest Central Committee members to come to Nanjing early to discuss national affairs together. As for the candidates and the number of personnel, nothing has been decided yet. Central Committee members have suggested sending Mr. Wu Zhihui and Mr. Dai Jitao to Hong Kong. However, this matter is still awaiting discussion and agreement by the members of the Central Standing Committee before seeking their consent.

Cracks Appear Within Fujian Province

Currently, the Southwest region's attitude towards the Fujian Incident is completely consistent with that of the central government. As for the internal affairs of the 19th Route Army, cracks have also been discovered, because most officers and soldiers of the 19th Route Army are unwilling to sacrifice their glorious history for personal gain. Therefore, Fujian is not only isolated, but also experiencing internal changes, so it should be possible to eliminate it in the short term.

According to the China East News Agency, Naval Fortress Commander of Mawei, Li Mengbin, refused to cooperate with the Fujian faction, which led to conflict with the Fujian faction. All the Jiangzhen, Jiangyuan, Chuguan, Haining, and other warships that were formerly berthed in Mawei were nearly besieged when the Changmen Fort was occupied. Now, Mr. Li has led the Jiangyuan and other warships to arrive at Sandu to concentrate and await orders. The Jiangzhen has escaped danger and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. After the warship Jiangzhen arrived in Shanghai, a reporter from China East News Agency paid a special visit to Vice Captain Wang Lunqin of the warship to inquire about the details. According to him, the details were quite detailed and are recorded as follows:

Seven Warships Berthing in Mawei Awaiting Orders

According to Mr. Wang, the Jiangzhen, Jiangyuan, and Chuguan warships were originally suppressing bandits on the sea surface bordering Fujian and Xiamen. The Jiangzhen also carried a battalion of marines. Since the bandits have been thoroughly suppressed, the pirates in the sea area have been gradually cleared out. Therefore, it returned to Mawei and berthed in the river. In addition to the warships that berthed at Mawei, there were also the Jiangyuan, Chuguan, Haining, Haiou and other gunboats, as well as the Jingliang and Qingyun surveying ships.

Tensions High: Prepare to Fire Up

On the afternoon of the 18th, the banknotes of the Central Bank in Fuzhou could not be exchanged because the bank was taken over. At the same time, the Fujian side issued an announcement. Commander Li Mengbin, who was stationed at Mawei Port, specially summoned the captains of the warships stationed at the port to talk about the changes in the political situation in Fujian Province. All warships should prepare themselves and fully refuel with coal and water. Prepare to fire up in order to cope with the situation.

Mr. Li Refuses to Cooperate with Fujian

That night (the 18th night), this warship suddenly received an order from Commander Li to immediately go to Sandu. After receiving the order, it immediately left Majiang. The next day (the 19th) it arrived at Sandu. After the warship left, Lin Heyuan and Rong Yinglin (mistaken for Yun Yinglin) and several adjutants sent by the Fujian side went to the fortress headquarters to meet Commander Li. Their intention was to invite Commander Li and the navy in Fujian to join the cooperation. Mr. Li rejected it on the spot, saying that he could not betray the central government. At this point, Lin and Rong left in disappointment. Commander Li knew that the time was critical, and because the marines were dispersed in various places for bandit suppression, it was difficult to gather them together in a short time. Therefore, Commander Li boarded the Jiangyuan warship in preparation for responding to the situation.

Resist for a Time, Fortress Occupied

On the 20th, the Fujian side sent troops to the fortress headquarters to take over. Because there were only a few guards in the headquarters, they retreated after a slight resistance. At this time, the Changmen Fort was occupied, because there was only a battalion of marines stationed there. The disparity in strength was too great. It is now reported that the Fujian side has placed six cannons and four aircraft in the fort. At this time, because the Changmen Fort had fallen, the Jiangyuan and other warships were nearly besieged. After escaping, Mr. Li led the Chuguan, Haining and other warships to Sandu for assembly.

The Haiou and Three Warships Were Indeed Detained

When Commander Li left Mawei, the Jingsing and Qingyun surveying ships and the Haiou gunboat in the inner harbor of Mawei were unable to withdraw, so they were detained. In addition, the personnel of the Majiang Shipyard have not withdrawn either.

Fujian Has Sent People to Be the Fortress Commander

It is rumored that he has been commissioned by Fujian Province as the commander of the Marine Corps. I don't know about that. The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong Plane Encountered Danger on Zhoushan Island Yesterday Morning. The Sikorsky S-16 Plane Carried Passengers for the First Time. It Fell Due to Heavy Fog on the Sea and Was Severely Damaged. The Company Sent a Medical Car to Zapu for Rescue

The China National Aviation Corporation's Sikorsky S-16 aircraft on the Shanghai-Guangdong route flew from Shanghai to Guangdong yesterday morning. Due to the bad weather and heavy fog, it turned back several times and finally encountered danger and crashed on the Zhoushan Islands. The company repeatedly sent planes to investigate and obtained confirmation. Then, it telegraphed and sent a medical car from Minhang to Zapu. It is not known whether the nine passengers and the American pilot, Mr. Rumil, were injured. Detailed reports have not been received until 10:30 PM. After hearing the news, the reporter met with Mr. Huang Jiangquan, Chairman of the Board, and Mr. Dai Enji, General Manager, to learn the details as follows:

The Encounter

China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong route, which travels back and forth between Shanghai and Guangzhou, has been in preparation for a long time. After a month of trial flights, it initially only carried mail and did not carry passengers. The trial operation was excellent. Only yesterday (24th) did it start carrying passengers. There were nine passengers. The new Sikorsky S-16 aircraft purchased from the United States was piloted by American pilot An Mu. It took off from Longhua at 6 AM. It turned back at 6:50 AM due to heavy fog. It took off again from the airport at 8 AM. It was not seen flying back at 9 AM. The company then telegraphed to inquire about the weather in Hangzhou and Wenzhou. The response was good, so it felt a little relieved. The company did not receive a radio report of the aircraft's whereabouts until 11 AM. The company then sent Mr. Ge Luoshu, director of the aviation group, to investigate by plane. He telegraphed back at 12:50 PM, saying that he had not found the whereabouts of the S-16 aircraft. It was not until 2:20 PM that he received a radio telegram from Mr. Ge, saying that he had discovered that the aircraft had crashed on the Zhoushan Islands in Zhejiang. Ge then drove back. He flew to Zhejiang again at about 4 PM to investigate. According to Mr. Ge's second telegram report,

The Rescue

Upon discovering the aircraft, the company immediately sent Chief Pilot Anderson to fly out. He flew back to Longhua at 5:30 PM. According to his report, the nine passengers had been helped by the local security corps and sent to the Zapu Hospital by civilian boats. After receiving the report, the company telegraphed Minhang and sent two medical cars to Zapu. The medical car left Min at 9:30 PM. It has not returned until 10:30 PM. According to General Manager Dai, the company has received a lot of help from all parties in Zapu in addition to the local security corps' efforts to assist after the aircraft encountered danger on Zhoushan Island. It is very promising.

Huang and Dai's Talks

According to Huang Jiangquan, Chairman of the Board of Directors of China National Aviation Corporation, and Dai Enji, General Manager, China National Aviation Corporation has been working hard on the aviation industry since its establishment. With the help of all parties, it has made rapid progress and has opened up the Shanghai-Chongqing and Shanghai-Beijing routes. There have been no accidents. This time, in order to connect the Shanghai-Guangdong transportation, the Shanghai-Guangdong route was officially carrying passengers for the first time today. Unexpectedly, due to the changing weather, this accident occurred, which is very regrettable. According to the S-16 aircraft, the manufacturing is extremely precise and strong. It was just purchased from the United States three months ago, and the equipment is quite complete. It uses dual motors and can fly an average of 120 miles per hour. Even if one motor is damaged, a single motor can still travel 85 miles per hour. It is also very stable. Pilot An Mu is American and has a lot of driving experience. This accident was really unexpected. However, accidents in aviation in various countries are not uncommon. The company sincerely hopes to deal with the aftermath properly and hopes that the Chinese people will understand.

Continued Injury Report

As the reporter was writing this article, he continued to be informed by China National Aviation Corporation by phone that there were a total of nine passengers in this accident. The more seriously injured were Yang Wenxin, the customs officer of Wenzhou Customs, and Miss Calase, the niece of British Ambassador Blue, and American pilot An Mu and Ehrnet were slightly injured. There were also Briton Reynald, German Schalser, and Chinese Yang Wenwu, Zhang Renwei, and Xu Da Jian, the eldest son of Xu Qianzhi, who were all fine.

Yesterday Catholic Parishioners Held a Memorial Mass for Xu Guangqi: Commemorating the 300th Anniversary of His Death, Representatives from All Walks of Life Participated

The achievements and deeds of Xu Wending, the Ming Dynasty's Prime Minister, are recorded in history. He was a close friend of Matteo Ricci and deeply studied astronomy and mathematics. His belief in Catholicism led to the establishment of the church in Shanghai, which he pioneered. Xujiahui is his hometown. Yesterday marked the 300th anniversary of his death. The Catholic Church of Xujiahui in Shanghai held a grand mass at 8:30 am in the Great Xujiahui Cathedral. At 3:00 pm, a memorial service was held at the tomb of Xu Wending in the southwest of the Xujiahui Cathedral. Invitations were sent to various circles to participate. Cross flags were erected along the road from the church to Xu's tomb, and security guards were stationed. A decorated archway and mat shed were erected in front of the tomb. Parishioners, family members, and nearby residents went to pay their respects and participate in the grand event. French Consul General Meyrier, Wu Mayor's representative and Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen, and leaders from all walks of life attended the ceremony. The event was magnificent. Before the ceremony, firecrackers were set off. Bishop Hui presided over the ceremony, and the order was as follows: (1) Guests enter and take their seats, music is played; (2) The Bishop enters and takes his seat, music is played; (3) National Anthem; (4) The Bishop holds a grand memorial service; (5) Memorial Prayer, music is played; (6) Eulogy for Xu Wending; (7) Speech by Priest Zhang Bo; (8) Speeches by guests; (9) The Bishop's closing remarks; (10) The Bishop and guests leave, music is played. The ceremony was entirely in accordance with Catholic rites. The meeting adjourned at 4:30 pm. Guests and parishioners went to the Catholic Church, had refreshments, and dispersed around 5:00 pm.

The recent situation in Fujian Province was serious and imminent. Sincerely, Chen Peikun and Wu Shan."

Resolutions

The meeting adjourned at around 6:00 pm.

The Ministry of Finance Continues to Borrow 1.5 Million Yuan from Shanghai Money Shops: The Money Shops Indicate That It Is Difficult to Comply

According to Dagong News Agency, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, due to the successive progress of the military campaign to suppress bandits and the post-war reconstruction of the recovered bandit areas, will use 5 million yuan of 22nd-year customs treasury bonds to borrow 2.5 million yuan in cash from Shanghai money shops to meet urgent needs. After the Money Shops Association convened an extraordinary meeting, it was resolved to lend 1 million yuan. On the 20th of this month, the money shops transferred the funds to the Money Shops Joint Reserve for remittance to the Ministry of Finance. According to reliable information obtained by the reporter of Dagong News Agency, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, considering that the expenses for suppressing the Red Army are enormous, in addition to borrowing 12.5 million yuan from the banking sector, at least 2.5 million yuan are still needed. At present, it is difficult for the money shops to agree to borrow 1 million yuan, but this is a drop in the bucket, or not a significant amount. Therefore, Finance Minister Kong sent another letter to the Money Shops Association a few days ago, requesting the industry to continue to borrow 1.5 million yuan in cash, so as to raise the original amount of 2.5 million yuan for payment. However, after receiving the letter, the money shops have indicated that they are unable to do so and it is difficult to comply. The reporter of Dagong News Agency inquired about everything from the Money Shops Association yesterday. The person in charge of the association replied that in recent years, due to the decline of commerce, the financial capacity of the money shops themselves has been affected by various factors and has repeatedly shown signs of exhaustion. This time, the Ministry of Finance borrowed 2.5 million yuan, and the money shops had already indicated that they were unable to handle it. After repeated discussions, the money shops reluctantly agreed to borrow 1 million yuan. The state treasury's deficit is important, but the difficulty of the money shops is also a reality. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance's request to borrow another 1.5 million yuan from the industry this time has made the money shops feel that they have done their best. It is difficult to comply and will politely explain the situation to the Ministry of Finance in the coming days, hoping to withdraw the order.

Postal and Telecommunications Merger Conference: Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Will Pilot First

According to Huadong News Agency, the Ministry of Transportation recently ordered the merger of the postal and telecommunications organizations to save on expenses for both, on the one hand, to provide convenience to the public, and on the other hand, to save expenses. The Shanghai Postal General Bureau and the Telegraph Bureau held a meeting at the Telegraph Bureau yesterday afternoon to discuss the progress of this matter. The result was that Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces will pilot first. If the results are good, it will be promoted to the whole country, and various implementation steps will be decided. The reporter of Huadong News Agency learned the details from all parties as follows: After the Ministry of Transportation's Postal General Bureau and Telegraph Bureau of this city received the order, they held a meeting at the Telegraph Bureau yesterday. Zhu Menghou, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Postal Bureau, attended, and the Telegraph Bureau also sent representatives from the National Route Management Office to discuss how to merge. It was decided that both parties would investigate the situation and then discuss it again. However, the principle of merger has been decided. Jiangsu and Zhejiang will be piloted first, because the transportation network in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces is the most developed and because they are located in a strategic location. Therefore, it is planned to pilot first, and then promote it to other provinces if the results are good. The Postal Bureau and the Telegraph Bureau are currently drafting detailed rules for implementation and are submitting them to the Ministry of Transportation for approval.

Economic Independence The merger of the postal and telecommunications systems is intended to save expenses and provide convenience to citizens, but the economic aspects of both parties will remain independent and will not be merged. As for the expenses, they will be borne equally by both parties. The Postal Bureau has stated in advance that the merger should not increase the burden. If the telegraph branch office moves into the post office building, the extra expenses incurred by the post office should be borne by the Telegraph Bureau.

Shao Lizi Passed Through Shanghai This Morning to Return to His Hometown: He Took a Train to Hangzhou and Then Returned to Shaoxing, Shao Delivered a Speech on the Train

According to Xin Xin News Agency, Shao Lizi, Chairman of Shaanxi Province, and his wife arrived in Shanghai by night express train yesterday (24th). After staying for more than an hour, they transferred to a train to Hangzhou and then returned to Shaoxing, their hometown. Shao told reporters at the station that his mother, Madam Zhang, passed away in May of the Republic of China's 14th year (1925), and nearly eight years have passed since then. He has been delinquent in not burying her. The reason is that he has been running around for years and has not had time to choose a burial place. His hometown is Shaoxian, and in Shaoxing, fields are often used as graves, which he has never advocated. It was not until he returned from Gansu this spring that he returned to Shao and chose a site in the mountains of Fusheng Township. He and his brother Boqian followed their late mother's lifelong thrift, love, and care, and decided to build a house nearby and start a rural primary school, and build a family cemetery near the tomb temple, named Tangsa Cemetery to commemorate their late father, Mr. Chengqi, who often called himself the owner of Tangsa during his lifetime. The funeral will be simple, and all superficialities will be abolished. No obituaries will be issued in advance, and no inscriptions or eulogies will be requested. He usually sees people soliciting inscriptions and eulogies, and he often does not know them. They repeatedly ask for help, adding to the extravagance, and some even have dozens of pages, bound into a thick volume. At this time of urgent difficulties, it is wrong to waste useful material resources on this kind of superficiality, and he does not dare to imitate it. After his mother passed away, he did not receive any money. This time, the funeral is simple and frugal. In the eyes of ordinary people, it seems extremely inappropriate as a son. He and his brother only want to do more beneficial things to comfort the spirit of their late mother. Therefore, if any relatives and friends offer generous gifts, please donate all of the cash to the fund for rural trivialities. In Shaanxi and Gansu provinces, he has already published a statement in Xilan Prefecture, and all of it will be transferred to charitable causes in those provinces. His ex-wife, Madam Tu Yuying, passed away 14 years ago and will also be buried on the same day.

At the same time, each scheduled ship transporting goods to Japan is fully loaded. The export volume in October reached 40,000 tons, the highest record since January of this year. Elder Mr. Wang Shengshan Passed Away: The Encoffining Will Be Held at the China Funeral Home Today

Mr. Wang Shengshan, a prominent figure in Shanghai, was a veteran diplomat who served as a counselor and consul general in various European and American countries in his early years, wearing the Jewel Stars of six countries, traveling to fifteen countries, his footprints almost all over the earth, and also served as the Zhejiang Negotiator twice, dealing with negotiations and recovering our country's rights to a great extent. He was particularly enthusiastic in supporting social charitable causes. When the May 30th Incident occurred, the students of St. John's College could not bear the humiliation of foreigners and declared their departure from the school. Mr. Wang took the lead in destroying his home to establish a school, generously donating dozens of acres of private land, and founded Guanghua University to recover educational rights, pioneering the establishment of education by the Chinese themselves. Over the past eight or nine years, he has cultivated talents and benefited the country and society. Mr. Wang died of illness at his residence in Shanghai on the 23rd of this month. When the school heard the news, all the teachers and students were deeply saddened and lowered the flag to half-mast for three days to express their grief. Mr. Zhang Yongni, the president of the school, will lead representatives of the faculty and staff and all the students to the China Funeral Home on Heger Road this afternoon to encoffin the body. Mr. Wang enjoyed the age of seventy-six. He was highly respected and admired by the society. At that time, there will be a scene of sorrow with plain cars and white horses.

Glrian Will Be Appointed Commander of the Trade Corps

Commander of the Trade Corps of the Public Concession, Thomas, has resigned after completing his term of office. It has now been decided to appoint Colonel F. R. W. Graham to succeed him. Colonel Graham is 49 years old and is currently the commander of the First Battalion of the British Army's Ulster Rifles, stationed in Palestine. From 1908 to 1912, he served in the British Army in West Africa. During the Great War, he served in France, Belgium, Greece, Serbia, Bulgaria, Turkey, and other places. From 1917 to 1918, he served in Egypt and was wounded twice. He received five commendations in official documents. In addition to receiving various assistance from England, he was also awarded the War Cross by France.

The Submarine Cable Across the River Has Been Laid: Pudong and the Concessions Have Been Connected by Telephone Yesterday, and a Submarine Cable Will Also Be Built in the Bailianjing Port, the Branch Is Arranging the Installation of New Equipment, and Dismantling and Assembling Will Begin Next Month

The new submarine cable across the river from the Bund on Fuzhou Road to Lanni Ferry in Pudong, installed by the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation, has been completed yesterday. Pudong and the concessions have been directly connected by telephone with the new line. The water line from Jiangbian in Gaochang Temple to Zhoujiadu on the opposite bank will continue to be laid this morning. The cable reconstruction project in Bailianjing Port will also be carried out. The Pudong Branch is arranging the installation of new equipment, and the installation of new equipment will begin next month. The details are as follows:

New Line Used for Telephone Calls Yesterday

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau negotiated with the Telephone Company of the Concessions and paid to recover the cross-border water line directly connecting the Bund on Nanjing Road to Pudong. Then, it installed two new submarine lines at the Bund on Fuzhou Road and Jiangbian in Gaochang Temple, directly connecting to Pudong. The line on the Bund on Fuzhou Road is connected to the telephone of the Concessions, and the line in Gaochang Temple is connected to the telephone bureau of the Chinese community. On the 21st, the Engineering Department sent dozens of workers, hired small fire trucks and two sampans, and first installed the water cable from the Bund on Fuzhou Road to the opposite bank of Lanni Ferry, and then dismantled the old line. It was completed yesterday morning. From 1:00 pm, Pudong and Concession users used the new line to directly connect to Shanghai. The cross-river line from Jiangbian in Gaochang Temple to the coal company wharf in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, will continue to be laid this morning. The new line can also be used for telephone calls at the beginning of next month.

Building Cables in Bailianjing

Bailianjing Port is an important river in the inland port of Pudong. Factories, warehouses, and wharfs are lined up on both sides, but transportation equipment is still lacking. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau intends to install telephone engineering to develop urban transportation. It was originally planned to use overhead lines for connection, but because the port surface is wide, the project would be quite expensive. Therefore, it was changed to install a submarine cable across the river. All the village materials have been prepared and will be officially started next month.

Branch Is Arranging the Layout

The Pudong Branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, located on Dongchang Road, Pudong, has been repaired by the bureau and is now completed. It is currently arranging the internal equipment and will be established within the month. An 800-door power supply switchboard has been transported to the Pudong Branch and has begun to be configured. New user equipment will be installed at the beginning of next month.

Direct Transportation Method for Coordinated Transportation Parcels between Shanghai and Hankou: The Ministry of Railways Sets Ten Measures to Be Implemented before December 1, Yesterday It Ordered the Railway Bureau to Comply

The Ministry of Railways believes that there are a large number of coordinated transportation parcels between Shanghai and Hankou, which are received and transferred repeatedly, and the procedures are complicated. It is now planned to use vehicles to directly transport them across the track, and ten direct transportation measures have been stipulated, which must be implemented before December 1 of this year. Yesterday, it specially ordered the Railway Bureau to comply with the procedures. The measures are recorded below: (1) Nine direct coordinated transportation parcel vehicles are required between Shanghai North Station and Dazhimen in Hankou. Three state-owned vehicles from the Pinghan Railway and two vehicles from each of the Jinghu, Jinpu, and Longhai Railways must be equipped with electric lights, wind brakes, and steam pipes. (2) These vehicles will each run one vehicle daily in opposite directions from Shanghai and Hankou, attached to the first or eleventh/twelfth train of the Pinghan Railway, the first or second train of the Longhai Railway, the first or second train of the Jinpu Railway, and the first or second train of the Jinghu Railway.

Direct Ferry

(3) These vehicles are exclusively used to carry coordinated transportation of parcels of the four railways or various parcels of this railway, mainly to load coordinated transportation of parcels as soon as possible. As for the parcels within this railway section, they are attached. When receiving and handing over coordinated transportation of parcels, all parties must strictly comply with the Ministry's issued measures for the acceptance and sealing of coordinated transportation of parcels. (4) For various parcels transported to stations where express trains do not stop, they should be handed over to the previous large station for collection and transfer. (5) The station and the escorting staff should fill in the handover certificate (format attached) when receiving and handing over parcels. If there is any damage, the handing over party should sign and seal in the additional notes column to clarify the responsibility, and the directors of both parties should seal as evidence and should not be arbitrarily signed to show caution. (6) The escorting personnel of these vehicles will be directly appointed by each railway to take care of the handover matters. (7) In addition to the dedicated escorting staff, who are responsible for the coordinated transportation of parcels, each railway will only load and unload parcels within its own section. (8) When the vehicles of each station drive to any railway, they should be subject to

Command Inspection

If any smuggling is found, it will be dealt with according to the regulations of the railway where it is located, and the business office of the railway in charge will be notified at the same time. (9) Each escorting staff should fill in the escorting manifest (Chinese) with carbon paper in five copies. The number of pieces, the name of the goods, the ticket number, the starting station or the end station, should be clearly filled in one by one. If there is any damage or error, the responsibility should be noted together. After the transportation is completed, the escorting staff will seal them separately in envelopes and send them to the business offices and coordinated transportation offices of the relevant railways for record. If any assistance occurs according to Article 8, the examining officer shall note the details of the discovery in the manifest, write his title, and affix a seal as proof. (10) The travel expenses of the escorting personnel sent by each railway shall be handled by the railway in charge.

Ministry Order Stipulations: Capital Ferry Crossing Fees

First-Class Goods Subject to 100% Surcharge; Goods of Various Government Agencies Calculated According to Grading Table

Regarding the matter of stipulating Yangtze River crossing fees for first-class and above goods transported by the Capital Railway Ferry, the Ministry of Railways yesterday specially instructed the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations to comply. The original text reads: "According to a telegram from the Jinpu Railway Administration Committee, the Yangtze River crossing fees for first-class and above goods transported by the Capital Ferry have not yet been stipulated. Furthermore, it is requested to indicate whether goods of various military and political agencies that are recorded on account, reduced in price, or free of charge, as well as military supplies or easily explosive goods, can cross the river, and how the crossing fees should be calculated and collected." In response, it is now stipulated that for goods with freight rates classified as first-class and above in the ordinary goods grading table that cross the river by ferry, the crossing fee should be calculated and collected based on the proportion of their revised freight rate exceeding the first-class goods freight rate, and then added to the first-class goods crossing fee. For example, goods with a doubled first-class rate should have their first-class goods crossing fee increased by 100%, and goods with a 50% increased first-class rate should have their first-class goods crossing fee increased by 50%. Furthermore, the crossing fees for goods of various military and political agencies that are recorded on account, reduced in price, or free of charge should be calculated according to the grade stipulated in the grading table. As for how to collect the crossing fees and whether explosives can cross the river by ferry, four detailed methods have already been stipulated in Instruction No. Ye Zi 6654, and all routes have been ordered to comply. The aforementioned request should be handled in accordance with the previous order. Based on the submission, all routes are hereby notified to comply. In addition to the directive, this order has been forwarded by the bureau to the Traffic Department for compliance.
