National Federation of Commerce Requests Addition of Two Township Telegraph Offices;

Jie Shou and Si Shui Townships in Northern Jiangsu; Approved by the Ministry Yesterday

The National Federation of Commerce, noting that the telegraph office in Jieshou Township, located on the border of Baoying and Gaoyou counties in northern Jiangsu Province, was suddenly removed during the dike breach in the autumn of the previous year, resulting in the severance of communication between tens of thousands of residents in the county's villages and townships and the outside world, causing significant delays, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Communications yesterday. They earnestly requested that the Jiangsu Telecommunications Administration restore the office and establish a telegraph office in Sishui Township, a more commercially developed area of Baoying County, to facilitate communication. The original telegram reads: "Respectfully to the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, a telegram from Yan Zuobin, Executive Committee Member of the association, stated that transportation in Baoying and Gaoyou counties in northern Jiangsu Province is obstructed, with no railways or long-distance buses available. Normally, communication relies solely on wired telegraphs and postal services. In the autumn of the previous year, due to the dike breach, the telegraph office in Jieshou Township, located on the border of Gaoyou and Baoying, was suddenly removed, causing a sudden severance of communication between approximately one hundred villages and townships within a radius of one hundred and several tens of li, inhabited by hundreds of thousands of residents, and the outside world. Furthermore, there are no fewer than thirty to fifty thousand individuals in the various villages and townships engaged in military, political, academic, industrial, and commercial activities outside the region. Whenever urgent matters arise requiring telegrams, they are helpless and unable to seek assistance, causing significant delays. It is hoped not only that the Jieshou Township telegraph office will be restored to alleviate the hardship of delayed urgent matters but also that a telegraph office will be established in Sishui Township, a more commercially developed area of Baoying County, to promote the development of communication and benefit agriculture, industry, and commerce, etc. Based on this, we hereby submit a telegram to your ministry for review and earnestly request that the Jiangsu Telecommunications Administration establish telegraph offices in Jieshou and Sishui townships to facilitate communication. This is of utmost importance." Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, bows.

Unemployed Silver Furnace Workers Petition Yesterday,

Presenting Three Demands;

Requesting Immediate Order to Industry Directors to Comply

Since the Ministry of Finance explicitly ordered all silver furnaces in Shanghai to cease operations, over a thousand unemployed workers, facing difficult living conditions, formed the Shanghai Silver Furnace Industry Unemployed Workers Group and repeatedly requested mediation and subsidies from the Municipal Party Headquarters. After more than a month with no resolution, the group sent forty representatives to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau again yesterday, submitting a petition to seek an early resolution. The details are recorded as follows:

Details of the Petition: Yesterday at 10:00 AM, the group sent forty representatives, including Jin Jiamao, led by their attorney Wu Yusheng, to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition. They were received by Section Chief Xu and Section Chief Wang Gang of the Mediation Division. Wu Yusheng presented the petition and submitted three demands: (1) Request that the industry directors be ordered to hand over all the union hall and productive property built by the workers' donations for sale and distribution to the unemployed workers for relief; (2) Request that the industry directors' unauthorized mortgage of 120,000 yuan in real estate be declared invalid; (3) Given the approaching cold weather, the workers have been unemployed for a long time and are suffering from hunger and cold. It is requested that the industry directors' representative Yao Daji be summoned to the bureau to guarantee compliance. Wang Gang indicated acceptance and promised to handle the matter as soon as possible. He also instructed the labor representatives to quickly compile a roster and thoroughly investigate and report all property for verification. At 11:00 AM, the group representatives, still led by Wu Yusheng, continued to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters, submitting the petition and demands. They were received by Lu Yinchu of the Civil Training Section, who agreed to immediately notify the Social Affairs Bureau by telephone to expedite the matter. The workers were satisfied and dispersed, also planning to thoroughly investigate the exact amount of the industry's assets for reporting and confiscation.

Text of the Petition: The petition presented by the group to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday is as follows: "Petition regarding industry directors occupying the union hall built by worker donations and mortgaging it for personal gain, urgently seeking relief." It is noted that the silver furnace industry, in compliance with the government's explicit order to abolish the tael and implement the yuan, has uniformly ceased operations. All unemployed silver furnace workers have specialized in this skill since childhood and have different circumstances from general workers changing professions. In October of this year, Jiamao and others petitioned for relief of unemployment, requesting that the industry directors sell the union hall and productive property (located at Chengda Lane, Jubao Li, 67 Tiantong Road, British Concession, consisting of a residential building and a public hall totaling 33 rooms, valued at over 30,000 yuan at current market prices) built by the workers' past wage donations and use the proceeds to compensate the unemployed workers. This is extremely simple and easy to accomplish. However, the industry directors forcibly occupied the union hall and refused to hand it over, colluding with one or two industry directors who were unaware of the situation to mortgage the union hall for 120,000 yuan. They returned half of the guaranteed deposit of 3,000 taels previously held by each silver furnace (i.e., 4,500 taels per furnace) to each furnace (traditionally, each silver furnace had to pay 3,000 taels to the guild when established, and half was returned upon closure). This time, the silver furnace closures were due to explicit government orders. Logically, returning 3,000 taels to each furnace would have been sufficient, but using their control of the property rights, they brazenly mortgaged it for 120,000 yuan, first recovering funds for the wealthy silver furnace owners, while the original donating workers requested uniform relief. They used various methods to perfunctorily delay. On the 3rd of this month, Jiamao and others were notified to invite the industry owner representative Yao Daji and others to the bureau to consult on everything in advance. Yao Daji and others, knowing that their reasons were unjust, agreed to provide concrete measures or further mortgage the property on the 10th of this month to provide relief to the unemployed workers. However, day after day passed with no news. Now that the weather is getting colder, they have been unemployed for a long time, their wives are crying, and their children are wailing, a tragic scene. The industry directors obtain funds for personal gain and each has their own wealth, but they stand idly by, regarding the situation as irrelevant. Jiamao and others are under unbearable pressure and are painfully exploited. They pen their grievances in tears, making a final plea, requesting your esteemed bureau to review and approve a meeting to express their grievances, promptly summoning the industry owner representative Yao Daji and others to the bureau for detention and requesting a letter to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court to seize the mortgaged union hall in advance, to prevent deception and provide relief."

Cigarette Industry Petition Representatives Return to Shanghai,

Minister Kong Promises Joint Remediation

Before the January 28th Incident, the Chinese cigarette industry had an annual sales increase of approximately 25%. Since the January 28th Incident, the market has been sluggish, and hand-rolled cigarettes and counterfeit cigarettes in various provinces have become increasingly prevalent. The impact of the tax increase in March of last year caused the machine-made cigarette business to plummet. Of the more than eighty cigarette factories in the past, only forty remain today, and only about twenty of them are still operating and barely maintaining their work. They are also worried and struggling to survive. The Chinese Cigarette Factory Industry Association, recognizing this critical situation, elected permanent committee members Wu Tingsheng, Bao Gengsheng, and Shen Weiting as petition representatives to go to Beijing and request the Ministry of Finance to quickly seek remedial measures. Minister Kong personally met with them and adopted the various points presented, promising to plan in detail and jointly seek remedies. The representatives, believing that the government intended to maintain the industry and that the cigarette factories may still have a chance of survival, returned to Shanghai to report and hold a meeting. The petition is recorded below. "Petition for Relief of the Cigarette Business and Regulations for Adjusting Machine-Made Cigarettes and Native Tobacco, Requesting Review and Approval." It is noted that the cigarette business has shown signs of decline since September 18th. After the Shanghai War reached a peace agreement, the tax increase order was issued again. Cigarette merchants had barely recovered and were unable to cope. However, given the urgent needs of the nation and the shortage of funds, they embraced the responsibility of every citizen and took patriotic measures to relieve the national crisis, reluctantly bearing the heavy taxes. However, since the tax increase on March 21st of last year, business has further declined. The reason is not only due to the sluggish social economy and the decline of rural areas, but the widespread use of hand-rolled native tobacco has also dealt a major blow to machine-made cigarettes. For example, in the eight provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, the native tobacco business is flourishing and difficult to eradicate. It is estimated that each province sells 1,500 boxes per month, with a total exceeding 10,000 boxes, which is alarming. Not only has the machine-made cigarette business suffered significant losses, but the reduction in tax revenue also amounts to 500,000 to 600,000 yuan per month. Moreover, the cigarette merchants' business has shrunk, but various expenses cannot be reduced, and the livelihood of the workers must be maintained. They are struggling to survive with great difficulty. If the production and sale of native tobacco can alleviate the livelihood of the poor, the resulting reduction in national tax revenue and the impact on the cigarette merchants' business rights are not worth the loss. Considering the advantages and disadvantages, it is felt that this is not a sustainable solution. Therefore, for mutual benefit, it seems that both sides should be considered. Here, we will briefly explain our views: (1) The current tax rate on hand-rolled native tobacco is lighter than that on machine-made cigarettes, but the actual tax payment is almost zero. Moreover, most native tobacco is counterfeit, directly infringing on the machine-made cigarette business. If this is not addressed soon, the machine-made cigarette industry will inevitably fail, native tobacco will rise to replace it, and national tax revenue will be significantly affected. This is not a mutually beneficial solution. The measures to address native tobacco are as follows: (a) The cigarette paper for machine-made cigarettes has always been white and should remain so in the future. (b) The cigarette paper for native tobacco, regardless of the color currently used, should be changed to yellow or blue in the future to facilitate distinction and prevent counterfeiting. (c) The native tobacco tax rate is set at 20 yuan per 50,000-cigarette box, but in reality, this is ineffective. The widespread use of native tobacco is closely related to this. Now, both for the sake of tax revenue and the machine-made cigarette industry, and for the sake of the livelihood of native tobacco farmers and the poor, it is proposed to reduce the native tobacco tax rate from 20 yuan to 10 yuan, or even 5 yuan, to make it easier to collect and prevent blatant tax evasion. If there are still violations or tax evasion, special provisions should be made to punish them accordingly. This approach would be both lenient and strict, ensuring that the production and sale of native tobacco does not affect national tax revenue and the machine-made cigarette business as severely as it does today. The credibility of government policies can also be maintained. The native tobacco tax can be added to the price of the cigarette paper (assuming each box requires 7 yuan of cigarette paper, add a 10 yuan tax, and sell the cigarette paper to native tobacco merchants for 17 yuan). The Tax Bureau will allocate funds to purchase the cigarette paper so that native tobacco merchants can purchase it from the local tax collection agencies. If they purchase it from others, it will be considered tax evasion. This procedure is simple and thorough, and tax revenue can be collected. It is truly a win-win situation, benefiting both the nation and the people. The impact of native tobacco on the machine-made cigarette business has been described above, and the increase in tax rates has also had a significant impact. Since the tax increase, the business has sharply declined, and the cigarette merchants have suffered losses. The unified tax revenue has also decreased. In areas that still operate under the old tax rate and have no tax evasion, the business is booming and tax revenue is increasing. They cannot be compared on the same day. Now, for the sake of the machine-made cigarette business and national tax revenue, it is proposed to restore the tax rate to the level before March 21st of last year, so that cigarette merchants can reduce their burden. If the tax rate is reduced and measures are taken to address native tobacco, the machine-made cigarette business will gradually return to its original state, and national tax revenue will also increase. Therefore, from the current situation, whether for the sake of tax revenue or cigarette merchants, it is necessary to adjust the tax rates on machine-made cigarettes and native tobacco. After the machine-made cigarette business recovers and is able to handle the burden, then further tax increases can be discussed, which can be promoted and fully implemented without causing public and private difficulties. The association is concerned about national tax revenue and the cigarette merchants' business and dares not remain silent. We respectfully submit this document, requesting your esteemed Minister to adopt and implement it to benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. We are the people who have this concern." Respectfully submitted to the Minister of Finance, submitted by Wu Tingsheng, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Industry Association.

Armed Robbery on Jessfield Road

At around 10:00 PM last night, the home of Wang Zuojin, an Anhui native who owns the Wang Zhenchang Weaving Factory at No. 67 Qianjia Lane, Jessfield Road, Shanghai, was suddenly visited by four robbers speaking with a Jiangbei accent. High Second Branch Court

Tries Key Members of "Dog Beating Gang,"

Citing Complex Circumstances, No Outside Observation Allowed;

Western Detective Insults Reporter, Greatly Lacking Discretion;

Suspects Not Yet Sent to Public Security Bureau for Investigation

Shanghai Public Security Bureau detectives previously arrested Cheng Xiangping (aka Chen Xiangping), a key Communist Party suspect, at the Xiaodongmen Central Hotel. Cheng confessed that accomplices were hiding in the Public Concession. Detectives from the Public Security Bureau immediately joined forces with Chinese and Western detectives from the Laoza Gate Police Station to arrest six accomplices - Ou Zhiguang, Zhang Yushan, Yuan Youfang, Zhang Dexin, Dong JiQuan, and a woman, Chen Zhang - in Room 40 of Longmen Road, Room 88 of Zaider Li on Chengdu Road, and Room 33 of the Zhongxing Hotel on Hankou Road. They seized seven pistols, four box cannons, three toxic gas pistols, two bombs, and over 1,000 rounds of ammunition, taking them back to the police station. Under interrogation, it was discovered that Ou and the other suspects had committed major crimes such as assassinations in the Concession. The next day, they were transferred to the High Second Branch Court. The Public Security Bureau prepared a document requesting their transfer, but the court ruled that because the suspects had committed major crimes in the Concession, it would expedite the interrogation by first concluding the Concession cases before transferring them to the Public Security Bureau. After investigation by the police, it was discovered that the defendants had a secret organization in the Concession called the "Dog Beating Gang," which aimed to assassinate political officials. They had committed eleven cases, including the murder of Huang Yonghua, director of the Public Security Bureau's Political Group, and his bodyguard Qian Rongqing, Central Commissioner Ma Shaowu (aka Lu Keqin), Gu Minghui, Wu Tian (aka Lei Dafu), and attempted assassinations of Zeng Boqian, Wu Xiu, Wang Shouxi, Hao Ming, He Jianqing, and a woman named Zhang Cao, all of whom were seriously injured. Yesterday morning was the scheduled trial date. At 10:00 AM, Yu Hua, the Criminal Division Chief of the High Second Branch Court, opened Criminal Division One to conduct the trial. Beforehand, the Public Security Bureau received a notification from the police, so they commissioned legal advisor James Ki Fong to attend the court with inspectors. Lawyer Li Zhishan represented the Municipal Council. Li Zhishan first stated that because the defendants were an important Communist Party group, he requested that public observation be prohibited. Judge Yu granted the request and ordered the spectators to leave. As the reporter rose from the seat and prepared to leave the courtroom, Logen, a Western detective from the Laoza Gate Police Station, suddenly stepped forward, pushed the reporter, and shouted in English, "Get Out!" Upon hearing this, the reporters believed that the power to maintain order in the courtroom belonged to the bailiffs and that the detective should not have intervened. Furthermore, the reporter had already risen from the seat and was about to leave, so the detective's harsh words were an insult to the reporter's dignity. They immediately questioned him, at which point Judge Yu heard the disturbance and asked Lawyer Li about the truth. The reporter explained the situation, and Judge Yu stated, "Since the police have requested to prohibit public observation, please leave the court." To respect the court's instructions, the reporter immediately left. Because the case was exceptionally complex, the trial took a considerable amount of time, so the suspects were not immediately sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Gasoline Price Increase Rumors

Soviet Oil Company to Reach Agreement with Anglo-American Oil Companies;

Those Enjoying Cheap Gasoline May Feel Disappointed

The Continental Daily News reports that there are widespread rumors that Soviet Oil Company "Oil Everywhere" and Anglo-American Oil Companies in the Far East will soon reach an agreement. If this rumor is true, the period of cheap gasoline for car owners in Shanghai will soon end. Although people from Oil Everywhere and Anglo-American Oil Companies are denying that an agreement has been reached or will be reached soon, the rumor of a kerosene price increase occurred recently and was realized at the end of last week, with the price increasing from 5-5.2 yuan per ten gallons to 5.7 yuan. Now, there are rumors that Oil Everywhere, Mobil, Texaco, and Asiatic companies will reach an agreement by the beginning of December at the latest to increase gasoline prices. It is undeniable that Shanghai's gasoline prices are unusually low due to competition, and selling companies are losing several cents per gallon. It is also obvious that this suicidal policy cannot last indefinitely. Furthermore, since the merger of the Far East operations of the two companies represented by Mobil in September, they have been in a position to compete with other companies. At that time, there was talk that this could stabilize the Far East oil market. Although gasoline prices did not rise, they avoided further price cuts. Therefore, the price of 70 cents per gallon in September has been maintained until today. Previously, Soviet oil prices would be reduced by another five cents each time Anglo-American gasoline prices were cut to compete. As a result, the price fell from 1.30 yuan per gallon in the spring to 70 cents. The price war among oil companies in the Far East was originally started by Russian oil wanting to occupy a larger share of the Chinese market. The United States' recognition of the Soviet Union is expected to help resolve the dispute between the two countries' kerosene industries.

Domestic Fruit Exported to England for Promotion

Shipment by Ship Next Month

Initially Testing Sales of Chestnuts, Pears, and Ginkgo Nuts

Sudden Outbreak of Fujian Incident Affects Fruit Merchants

To develop China's foreign fruit trade, the Shanghai International Trade Bureau previously convened fruit merchants to discuss ways to expand business. It was decided to first test sales of chestnuts and ginkgo nuts in England. Fruit merchants have been actively preparing. It is learned that preparations have been completed and shipment by ship to England will begin next month. The details are recorded as follows:

Shipment Next Month: A reporter from the Dagon Association met with Mr. Zhu of the Fruit Industry Association, who said that the shipment of ginkgo nuts, pears, and other fruits to England for promotion has been decided. Three tons will be shipped initially for testing. They will be packed in wooden boxes, with lengths, widths, and thicknesses similar to those popular in the British market. Once the color advertisements are printed, shipment will begin next month. All customs clearance procedures have also been arranged.

Not Considering Profit or Loss: The English are fond of Chinese-produced chestnuts, with several hundred tons shipped to England from Singapore each year. Unfortunately, these are mostly sold by foreigners, and there is very little direct trade between Chinese and British merchants. Chestnuts account for most of these fruit exports. The fruit merchants only seek to expand sales and do not consider profit or loss. If necessary, they will send personnel to England to promote the advantages of Chinese fruits.

Impact of Fujian Incident: The oranges and olives sold in Shanghai are mostly imported from Fujian. Since the outbreak of the Fujian Incident, the supply has been cut off. Ships traveling between Xiamen and Shanghai, originally from Sanbei, China Merchants, Jardine Matheson, Chang'an, and other shipping companies, are now all suspended except for Jardine Matheson. If foreign ships are used to transport the fruits in the future, the shipping costs will be high, and the loading and unloading methods of foreign ships are inadequate. Therefore, Fujian-produced fruits may soon disappear from the market.

Zhao Guirong Bravely Arrests a Thief and Loses His Life; The Thief Comes Face to Face and Shoots Him

Zhao Guirong, a native of Funing, was 39 years old and worked as a laborer. He lived at No. 7, Tianfu Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei. On the evening of the 20th of this month, at around 6 p.m., Zhao suddenly heard his neighbor shouting about a robbery. He bravely rushed out of his house and saw a thief running wildly towards him. Zhao went forward, intending to capture him. Unexpectedly, the thief, in desperation, pulled out a pistol and fired several shots at Zhao, all hitting vital spots. Zhao fell to the ground, covered in blood and unconscious. The thief took the opportunity to escape without a trace. His family then took Zhao to Baolong Hospital in the British Concession for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died of his injuries the day before yesterday. The hospital reported this to the Xinzha police station, which ordered detective Chen Shanji to investigate. The body was then taken to the forensic examination office on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, was dispatched to the office to examine the body. After questioning Zhao Huang, the deceased's wife, who recounted the events, Guo concluded that the deceased Zhao Guirong died from gunshot wounds sustained during his lifetime. The body was handed over to his wife, Zhao Huang, who signed a document promising to arrange for the coffin and burial. It is understood that the authorities of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau in the Chinese area have arrested one thief since the incident occurred and are now strictly pursuing his accomplices.

Articles of Association of the Association

Articles of Association of the Shanghai Beggar Relief Association. (1) Name: This association is named the Shanghai Beggar Relief Association. (2) Purpose: This association, based on the principle of division of labor and cooperation, aims to eliminate beggars in Shanghai. (3) Organization: This association is organized jointly by various charitable organizations and enthusiastic individuals in Shanghai. (4) Officers: This association shall have fifteen executive committee members, and seven standing committee members shall be elected from among the executive committee members. (5) Funding: The sources of funding for this association are: (1) Requesting subsidies from the government, (2) Utilizing production methods, (3) Soliciting donations from society. (6) Meeting Schedule: The meeting schedule for this association is: (1) Executive Committee Meeting: once a month, (2) Standing Committee Meeting: once every half month, (3) If there are urgent matters, temporary meetings may be convened. (7) Address: Temporarily located at No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road, Room 508. (8) If these articles of association are not perfect, they may be amended by a proposal from three or more committee members and approved by a majority of the committee members.

Shangchuan Automobile Adds Special Bus Services and Reduces Second-Class Fares

Shangchuan Automobile, as a general rule, from October 16th to March 15th of the following year, due to the gradual shortening of daylight hours, reduces one morning and one evening bus service. Now, the company believes that after the reduction of services, the arrival time in Shanghai for passengers from Chuansha and Nanhui is at 10 a.m., and those engaged in industry and commerce feel inconvenienced as the office hours have already passed. After investigating the situation, it seems necessary to add services. It has now been decided that from December 1st, a special bus service will be trialed once each from Chuansha Station at 7 a.m. and Qingning Temple Station at 8 a.m. Moreover, it has been found that most of the passengers on these buses are workers and various merchants in Shanghai. In these times of economic recession, although the original fare is already low, those who pay still find it difficult. The company, while facilitating transportation, also favors the common people. Therefore, a special fare for the special bus service has been set at 3.2 cents from Chuansha to Qingning Temple (a reduction of 1 cent from the original fare), with successive reductions for other stations. The same applies from Qingning Temple to Chuansha. However, this is limited to second-class and long-distance fares, while first-class and short-distance fares remain at the original price. It is said that negotiations have been held with the Municipal Ferry Management Office for joint tickets, and a report has been submitted to the Public Utilities Bureau for record.

All incoming and outgoing cargo is transported by iron barges. The Honor of the Xinyi Pharmaceutical Factory

The Shanghai Masnan Road Xinyi Chemical Pharmaceutical Factory is the most perfect of the pharmaceutical factories established by Chinese people themselves. The talents are outstanding, and the various injections, oral medications, and external medicines produced have achieved outstanding results, comparable to imported products. It has long been famous and is popular with the police. In particular, Vita Cibaoming pills and injections have long been known throughout society. Even working day and night, they are still overwhelmed. It has recently been learned that the factory has specially sent expert technicians to the United States to study pharmacy in order to further their education and has purchased the latest equipment and machinery from the world's largest pharmaceutical factories in America, which has not been seen by our people. Most of it has already arrived in Shanghai and been installed, at great expense. The Vita Cibaoming produced by the factory, its Cibaoming cross-shaped endocrine crystals, and Wuling ovarian follicular endocrine crystals are unique products on the Chinese new drug market. In particular, the success of type B vitamin crystals caused a sensation at the time, as this type of crystal is still the latest invention in the world of science, and the factory succeeded first, which is worthy of praise. For this reason, both Chinese and Western physicians praised it, and the factory is the light of domestic new drugs.

Famous Comedian Ding Guai Guai Commits Suicide by Hanging; It is Said to Be Due to Economic Pressure

Ding Guai Guai, 51 years old, who enjoyed great fame with the comedian Liu Chunshan of the trend and the late old comedian Wang Wuneng, was from Hangzhou, Zhejiang. He resided in the front building of the second floor at No. 41, Taihe Lane, Bai'erbu Road, French Concession. He is currently performing comedy stand-up at the Tianyun Building Game Hall on the roof of the Wing On Company. Recently, due to economic constraints, he suffered from neurological disorders that recurred from time to time. Yesterday, Ding was at home, taking advantage of the fact that his wife, Wang (46 years old, from Zhenjiang), had gone to visit their daughter, he was alone at home. In the afternoon, his illness relapsed again, and he suddenly had a suicidal thought. He used a rope to hang himself from the beam in the room behind the building, closing the door. It was not until 4:30 p.m., when the Wing On Company was waiting for him to go on stage, that he had not arrived for a long time. His apprentice, Sanbin, called by phone. The maid Wang Chen, who lived with the second landlord, answered the phone and went upstairs to call Ding, but there was no response for a long time, and the door was tightly closed. She then called the second landlord, Su Ming, to pry open the door and check. Ding was hanging himself. They immediately untied him, but it was too late because he had already stopped breathing. The second landlord reported to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. After the police photographed the hanging body, the body was taken to the Second District Yuansheng Hall Forensic Examination Office for an examination. Today, it will be reported to the Second District Court for an examination before the body is prepared for burial. Ding had two sons and two daughters. The eldest son, Zhi Xin, is 25 years old, and the youngest son, Xiaoguai, is only four years old. The eldest daughter, Fengying, also earns a living by performing Tan Huang, and the second daughter, Yueying, is 21 years old. His funeral is extremely desolate, and many in the same profession pity him.

Red Pill Facility Cracked Down on Nanxun Road; Organized by Japanese Colluding with Chinese

Lu Liankui, Chief Chinese Inspector of the General Inspectorate, learned that a Western-style house at No. 9 Nanxun Road was a large-scale opium substitute, red pill production facility, operated jointly by Japanese and Chinese. He obtained a search warrant from the court and notified the Japanese authorities. At around 7 p.m. the day before yesterday, he collaborated with West Detective Bo Pu, Chinese Detectives Liu Shaokui, Feng Zhiming, Song Bingzheng, and Japanese detectives from the police station to secretly raid the address. The house was a four-story Western-style building. They went straight up and found the door on the third floor locked, knowing that it was the location of the red pill production. They broke through the door and entered. The workers were busy collaborating and working very hard. They arrested workers Wu Qingsheng, Tan Afu, Dong Changsheng, Chen Acheng, Li Youle, Qiu Yuzhang, Wang Yulin, Wang Jinyi, and workers Wang Henian and Zhang Shengfa from the neighboring No. 10 Japanese residence, totaling ten people. They seized tens of thousands of red pills, worth a lot of money, as well as manufacturing equipment, iron pots, and drug materials. Together with the Japanese man named Abe Dokichi, they were taken to the Hongkou police station. The Japanese Abe was sent to the Japanese consulate for questioning, and Wu Qingsheng and others were detained. Yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation and said that the defendants admitted at the police station that they were all manufacturing drugs at the facility. All the old workers were on the run. The Japanese Abe Dokichi directed the work, and the production of red pills was also done by the employer. These red pills were named "Senma Brand," and each large package contained 10,000 pills, which were widely sold on the market. He presented some of the machinery and two packages of Senma brand red pills that had been assembled for inspection, saying that there were still various iron pots, equipment, and red pills, the number of which was quite large, and it was inconvenient to bring them to court. It would be best to invite the court to conduct an on-site inspection. Judge Liu Yugui questioned each defendant and ordered them to be returned to custody for further investigation.

Evil Procuress Abuses Prostitute to Death; Final Verdict in Third Trial: Imprisonment for Fifteen Years

Shi Zhang, a woman from Songjiang who previously lived in a pavilion room at No. 136, Tongzhi Lane, Aigre Road, French Concession, was 40 years old this year. She previously had several prostitutes in her home, who specialized in attending customers in various Han Zhuang. One of the prostitutes who sold herself, a woman named Xu Renbao from Liyang, was not good at catering to customers, resulting in a sluggish sex trade. This angered the evil procuress Zhang, who used cruel and vicious means to abuse and beat Renbao in every possible way, and also burned her with candle flames. As a result, she developed sores all over her body and was also stopped from eating, lying sick in bed. Unexpectedly, she was still often beaten to hasten her death. On April 10th of last year, she was discovered by a detective from the French police station, who detained Shi Zhang and sent her to the Second Special District Court, where she was prosecuted for injury. Renbao was sent to the hospital for treatment, but she died due to her serious injuries and illness. She was only 18 years old at the time of her death. Later, the police also changed the articles of prosecution and were sentenced to eight years imprisonment for injuring a person to death. Zhang refused to accept this and filed an appeal to the Higher Third Branch Court. After the trial, it was ruled that Zhang had intentionally committed murder, and the charge was changed to murder, with a sentence of life imprisonment. Zhang still refused to accept this and filed another appeal to the Supreme Court in Nanjing. This has been going on for a year and a half. Now, the Supreme Court has concluded the third trial and changed the sentence to 15 years of imprisonment for injury resulting in death. The judgment has already been delivered, and she will be sent to prison soon.

Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association Asks to Preserve the Space of the Lihao River

The Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association sent a quick mail telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, the Yin County Government, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner's Office, and the Former Ningbo Property Clearance Office, saying: "According to a letter from the Yinxian Xianghao River River Works Post-Disaster Office, the city base along the Lihao River in Yin County has now been transformed into a ring road. There are still several feet of space between the road and the stone revetment along the river. It is said that the Former Ningbo Property Clearance Office has plans to auction off the land. It is found that the Lihao River is a gathering place for boats from the western part of Yin County and Fenghua. The loading and unloading of passengers and goods is extremely crowded. During the Republic of China in 1928, the local citizens presented to the municipal government to raise huge sums to repair the river after dredging, and then laid stone revetment to facilitate pedestrians and convenience of loading and unloading. The remaining space was originally planned to be planted with trees to provide a resting place for pedestrians. Now, due to the storage of goods and the flow of pedestrians, it has become a necessary land for the port. If the market is implemented and municipal houses are built, the transportation of the port will be adversely affected, and the land is not even a foot wide, one side facing the river and the other side next to the main city road. If buildings are built, it will hinder the view of the city. The boatmen from all the villages and Fenghua have donated money to the river dredging and revetment project, and they are extremely opposed to this move. For the sake of municipal administration and public opinion, it is necessary to reserve the land. Therefore, the association asked to take charge and quickly send telegrams to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner's Office, and the Yin County Government to stop the auction plan in order to maintain traffic and comply with public opinion. Sincerely awaiting orders," The Lihao River is indeed an important port for navigation in the western part of Yin County and Fengyi, and it occupies an important position in transportation. The claim that the land should be reserved for the sake of municipal administration and transportation is a legitimate one. According to the previous letter, in addition to sending telegrams, we urgently ask you to review and take charge, and quickly order the property office to stop the auction, which is a public convenience. Yu Hede, etc., of the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, respectfully,

Mongolian Border Northwest Exhibition to be Held at the People's Education Hall Starting Tomorrow

Shen Yiqian, Gu Tingpeng, Zhang Yu, and other students from the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts organized a National Crisis Propaganda Group this spring and went to North China, Northwest China, and Inner Mongolia to promote their cause. They also drew various sketches of the places. They plan to borrow the People's Education Hall on Wenmiao Road, Ximen, to hold an exhibition to promote their work. The details are as follows:

Mongolian Border Sketches

The group members are enthusiastic about researching the border areas and are also proficient in painting. Since organizing the National Crisis Propaganda Group and using art as propaganda, they have traveled through eleven provinces, covering 20,000 miles, and returned south in the autumn. They held an exhibition in Beijing, which was praised by all parties in Beijing. All the materials are mostly those that were not available in the previous exhibition. The depiction of Mongolian customs and conditions is quite vivid and can be used for reference by those who study Mongolia and are concerned about the situation on the border.

Exhibition for Seven Days

The organizer of the exhibition obtained an introduction from Mr. Zhang Yichen last month and planned to borrow the exhibition hall opposite the New World Company on Nanjing Road, but it was canceled due to other difficulties. Yesterday, the head of the group, Shen Yiqian, went to the People's Education Hall and discussed with the director of the hall, Mr. Chen Songchun, and obtained his agreement to borrow four or five exhibition rooms for the exhibition. There are more than 300 works from Mongolia and Northwest China, most of which are sketches of Inner Mongolia, as well as sketches of Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, Hebei, Shanxi, and Shaanxi, photography, text records, local product collections, etc., which are all rare and valuable materials. It will be exhibited for seven days from the 26th.

Jianghai Customs Fines on Qiongzhou Sugar Case: Sugar Guild Cables Ministry of Finance to Appeal

The Qiongya sugar merchants transported domestic sugar to Shanghai, but the Jianghai Customs claimed it was mixed with foreign sugar and imposed a heavy fine. The merchants have been appealing for a long time, but there has been no result. It is now learned that the local Sugar Guild believes that this measure by the Customs is tantamount to destroying domestic sugar, and has sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting correction. The original telegram is recorded below:

To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing:

We have learned that the domestic sugar transported to Shanghai by Qiongya sugar merchants has been verified as genuine by the Beihai Customs. However, the Jianghai Customs insists that it is mixed with foreign sugar and has imposed a heavy fine, causing the sugar merchants to be fearful and dare not transport it anymore. We believe that domestic sugar is in the process of gradual recovery, and it is appropriate to support and cultivate it to promote its revival in order to achieve self-sufficiency and save foreign exchange. However, the Jianghai Customs has used the excuse of mixing with foreign sugar to arbitrarily impose fines. Is this not equivalent to promoting foreign sugar and helping its dumping? The future of domestic sugar is unimaginable. The guild has repeatedly reviewed the rationality of the merchant's appeals and deeply feels that the Jianghai Customs' measures are inappropriate and should be corrected immediately to show encouragement. However, for half a year, we have not received a correction from the ministry, and the fined money has not been ordered to be returned, causing the merchants to suffer immensely. The guild is concerned about domestic sugar and cannot help but feel apprehensive. Therefore, we earnestly appeal to the ministry to show compassion for domestic sugar, heed the requests of the Qiongya merchants, and make corrections. The future of domestic sugar may depend on it.

With utmost gratitude,

Shanghai Sugar Industry Guild

Record of the Postal Workers' Union Congress

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held its 11th Second Representative Congress on the 23rd. 115 representatives attended, with Zhang Kechang as chairman. The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting. Zhu Xuefan, representative of the National Postal Workers' Union, delivered a speech. The Executive Committee reported on the union's affairs. The discussion items were:

(A) The recent postal authorities have been oppressing local unions and repeatedly attempting to actively destroy the unions. How should the union deal with this?

Resolution:

(1) Vow to resist to the death and hand it over to the Executive Committee for full handling. All members will absolutely support the union and defend it to the end, taking action when necessary.

(2) Request the General Union to order local unions to strictly organize and be ready to act in unison.

(3) In order to enrich the union's finances, when the annual bonus is issued at the end of this year, 3% of the salary will be collected uniformly as a supplementary fund.

(B) The Hankou postal authorities have illegally punished and dismissed Chief Li Liqiang. How should the union express its support?

Resolution:

(1) Request the General Union to continue to negotiate with the authorities and immediately reinstate him. The efforts will not stop until the goal is achieved.

(2) Send a letter of condolence to Li Liqiang in the name of the Representative Congress.

(C) The Executive Committee proposed to formulate the budget for various income and expenditures for this session. Please submit it for discussion.

Resolution: Passed.

(D) The union library stipulates that a deposit of one yuan should be collected for borrowing drawings. Is this appropriate? Please vote on it.

Resolution: Passed.

(E) Regarding the establishment of a South District Club, the union's design department has prepared a plan. Is it approved to be held? Please discuss.

Resolution: Approved to be held, with a monthly allocation of 50 yuan for recurring expenses.

(F) The union's magic stock was suspended by the 10th Representative Congress due to the national crisis. Now, according to the request of the stock members to resume it and allocate monthly recurring expenses, how should it be handled? Please discuss.

Resolution: Approved to be resumed, with a monthly allocation of 5 yuan for recurring expenses.

(G) The violin class was originally organized by members voluntarily. Now, they intend to request the union to grant a monthly subsidy at its discretion. How should it be handled? Please discuss.

Resolution: A monthly subsidy of 5 yuan will be given.

(H) The 33rd sub-branch requested a monthly subsidy of 10 yuan for sports and entertainment expenses. Please discuss.

Resolution: Approved to grant a monthly subsidy of 5 yuan, to be transferred by the union's sports section.

(I) Executive Liu Xinquan et al. proposed that the 10th Representative Congress requested a plan to revise the current pension regulations and specially signed opinions. Please submit it for discussion.

Resolution: Handed over to the Executive Committee's design department for detailed planning and then submitted to the next congress for discussion.

The meeting was adjourned.

Overseas Paris: The Course of the Chinese Painting Exhibition (1)

(Paris Correspondence) The Sino-French University's office in France has prepared a report on the course of the Chinese painting exhibition in Paris, which is quite detailed. It is recorded below in sections.

In the winter of the 15th year of the Republic of China, Mr. Xu Beihong carried a part of his works and passed through Lyon. The colleagues of the Sino-French University asked him to hold a public exhibition, but he did not agree, and only displayed it in a room for people to view, which was highly praised by Chinese and foreign people. In the summer of the 19th year, Mr. Xie Shoukang was sent to Belgium and brought his works on his behalf, and held a "Xu Beihong Individual Exhibition" in this capital, which caused a sensation. After the exhibition, he also came to visit in person. In October of the same year, Mr. Hua Dabi transported Xu's works, except for those that had been sold in Belgium, to Zhi, and added a part of the products borrowed by Mr. Chu Minyi for China to participate in the Exhibition celebrating the Centennial of Belgian Independence. On the occasion of the Double Tenth Festival, it was displayed at the Lyon Sino-French University. Within three days, more than 4,000 people visited, and the newspapers gave enthusiastic publicity, and the reputation was very high. However, the people in Paris, the center of art, sighed that they had missed the opportunity. At the same time, the comrades in the academic circles of our country felt that Chinese art was quite necessary to be publicized abroad, so there was the brewing of the two exhibitions of Sino-German and Sino-French. In the summer of the 21st year, Mr. Li Shizeng came to Europe and then received a letter from Mr. Xu Beihong on August 7, which said that the Sino-French Painting Exhibition must be held, and entrusted Brother Hua Dabi to prepare everything and asked Mr. to discuss it with the French authorities. The main points are: (1) It must take the name of the Exhibition of Modern Chinese Art Collection of the Sino-French University in order to collect works; (2) It can be not open to the public to avoid disputes and the trouble of worthless works requiring to be added to the exhibition; (3) It is completely hosted by the Sino-French parties, and no irrelevant people participate. If it is approved, please show it before October, etc. On the same day, he sent the same letter to Mr. Liu Dabi, advocating that the National Museum of Modern Art of France, Roude Paume (TeudePaume, hereinafter referred to as Baum), should be the site of the exhibition, please urge it to be successful, and advise him to continue his efforts in foreign cultural undertakings, saying that returning is of no help to the crisis, etc. After receiving the letter, Mr. Li Shizeng extremely agreed, but advocated cooperation with the Sino-German Painting Exhibition and hosted by academic and art groups at home and abroad (such as Shanghai World Academy, Nanjing Central University, Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts, National Peiping Research Institute, Peiping Sino-French University, Suzhou Art School, Sino-French University's office in France, etc.) in order to strengthen the strength and facilitate the progress. In addition to replying to Mr. Xu by telegram, urging him to actively prepare, he also asked Mr. Liu Hou to postpone the return date to complete this task. This is the course of the preparation of the Sino-French Painting Exhibition. The organization of painting exhibitions by Chinese in France has been restored three times, but it has not been realized. The French side is very disappointed. This time, in the negotiation with the French government, the site was first proposed by Mr. Li Shizeng to Mr. Bo Lai, the president of the Paris World Academy, who agreed, and then instructed the secretary of the art department of the academy, Feng Du Jidi Si, to discuss with the French Deputy Minister of Art Education, Miss Lai, and the Director-General of the National Museum of Art, Mr. Fan Na. At first, Mr. Mi Fan and others were quite skeptical. After Mr. Liu's multiple explanations, Mr. Fan introduced him to Mr. Du Samaru, the curator of the Baum Museum. At that time, Mr. Du earnestly asked whether our association's organization funds had been settled, whether the morning exhibition works could represent Chinese art, and whether this organization could avoid repeating the previous mistakes, etc. He ordered several terms as left:

(1) The first floor of the Baum Museum is completely borrowed,

(2) The three exhibitions are scheduled between April 15th and May 15th,

(3) The pieces of the array must be selected representative works of pure Chinese art, which have not been Europeanized or Orientalized. The paintings must be 250 to 300 pieces, and they must be transported to France before March 15th.

(4) In addition to modern paintings, collect a number of ancient paintings, about to be displayed in a small room, for visitors to study the comparison of Chinese ancient and modern art,

(5) In addition to paintings, such as modern sculptures, porcelain, etc., those that can be representative works of the era should be collected and sent for display as much as possible.

(6) All organizational expenses are borne by the Chinese side. The catalog printing fee is allocated from the entrance ticket revenue. If there is any surplus, it should be paid into the French Treasury as usual.

The Baum Museum has two precedents for renting and borrowing. Renting means paying a monthly rent of 30,000 francs, and borrowing means that the entrance tickets of the exhibition are sold to them. At the beginning of our preparation for the painting exhibition, we suffered from the inability to pay the rent of 30,000 francs in advance, and we had no grasp of the results of the exhibition. At that time, we felt that borrowing the site was more free, but unexpectedly, the result was a great loss.

China: Standards for Passing Boy Scout Specialty Training (1)

The Preparatory Office of the Boy Scouts of China recently compiled standards for passing specialty training. These are recorded below:

(1) Citizenship: 1. Know a brief history of the Republic of China; 2. Know the organization of governments at all levels in the Republic of China; 3. Know the organization of the Kuomintang (Nationalist Party of China); 4. Know the system of judicial organs and the order of legal proceedings; 5. Know the general meaning of the "Fundamentals of People's Rights"; 6. Know the general meaning of the Five-Power Constitution; 7. Know the Local Autonomy Law; 8. Be able to speak fluent Mandarin.

(2) Writing: 1. Know the general structure of Chinese characters; 2. Be able to create common documents and know various official document formats; 3. Be able to write an article related to the Boy Scout movement; 4. Be able to write meeting minutes or a speech transcript; 5. Be able to stencil and mimeograph, or use a typewriter.

(3) Public Health: 1. Know the causes, symptoms, and prevention methods of infectious diseases such as scarlet fever, diphtheria, tuberculosis, meningitis, epidemic typhus, smallpox, cholera, dysentery, and influenza; 2. Know the harm of mosquitoes and flies, and fundamental methods of extermination; 3. Know the arrangement and disinfection of infectious disease rooms; 4. Know the importance of garbage removal and disposal methods; 5. Know how to keep food fresh in shops; 6. Be able to contact local health agencies to jointly engage in hygiene campaigns; 7. Be able to make sanitary products such as fly swatters and masks.

(4) Carpentry: 1. Be able to identify pine, fir, oriental pine, cypress, walnut, poplar, elm, teak, and chestnut wood, and know their uses; 2. Know the use and sharpening of woodworking tools; 3. Know various jointing methods and be able to create at least one type of mortise and tenon joint; 4. Be able to make a practical wooden object; 5. Know the construction method of wooden barracks.

(5) Repair: 1. Be able to paint a door or a piece of furniture; 2. Be able to whitewash walls or ceilings; 3. Be able to repair the locks of doors, windows, and cabinets; 4. Be able to repair two tents and tires, etc.; 5. Be able to furnish and repair interior decoration items; 6. Be able to sharpen knives and scissors, and manufacture small practical items; 7. Be able to cut and install window glass or paste paper; 8. Know the repair methods for cooking utensils and porcelain, etc.

(6) Leatherwork: 1. Know the method of making leather; 2. Be able to repair a pair of leather shoes; 3. Be able to attach leather soles to a pair of cloth shoes; 4. Be able to assemble a saddle and know how to repair it.

(7) Scouting Engineering: 1. Be able to tie ten knots in the dark or with eyes closed; 2. Be able to build a watchtower over six meters high; 3. Be able to construct at least three types of temporary river crossings in the field; 4. Be able to install military telephones; 5. Be able to build a shelter that can accommodate three or more people using natural materials.

(8) Printing: 1. Be able to set movable type and print small items such as flyers; 2. Know the names and sizes of lead type, and the types and sizes of paper; 3. Know the types of printing presses and how to use them; 4. Know the general principles of lithography.

(9) Bicycles: 1. Be able to ride a bicycle freely in streets and alleys at a speed of over fifteen kilometers per hour; 2. Be able to repair mechanical parts and tires, and know how to maintain and lubricate them; 3. Be able to disassemble and reassemble all mechanical parts; 4. Be able to deliver verbal messages according to a map.

(10) Automobiles: 1. Be able to drive automobiles and motorcycles and know the traffic rules; 2. Know the internal structure of automobiles and motorcycles; 3. Know small repair methods and maintenance methods for machines; 4. Be able to change tires and know how to repair inner tubes.

(11) Insects: 1. Know the morphology, life, properties, and benefits/harms to humans of forty types of insects; 2. Know at least ten types of pests harmful to crops and methods of extermination; 3. Know the methods of exterminating mosquitoes, flies, bedbugs, termites, fleas, lice, etc.; 4. Be able to lead or participate in insect extermination campaigns and write reports.

(12) Metalwork: 1. Be able to forge and weld iron bars three centimeters wide; 2. Know the procedures for smelting iron and the method of sand casting; 3. Know the method of steelmaking; 4. Be able to manufacture a practical item using metal.

(13) Masonry: 1. Know the mixing method of three-aggregate soil (sanhetu); 2. Be able to build a solid brick wall or lay a cement floor two meters square and be able to build a wall corner; 3. Know the use of spirit levels and plumb bobs; 4. Know the mixing and use of lime, sand, and paper pulp.

(14) Military Training: 1. Know the general military situations of the major powers; 2. Know the meaning of national defense and the basic organization; 3. Know the essentials of military science; 4. Have participated in more than one month of field training; 5. Know the use and maintenance of firearms and be able to shoot in the field; 6. Know various poisonous gases and defense methods; 7. Know military etiquette, symbols, and important military terminology; 8. Know the duties of army sentries, scouts, messengers, and liaison soldiers; 9. Be able to identify the types and missions of warships, tanks, and aircraft.

(15) Music: 1. Be proficient in at least one type of Chinese or Western musical instrument; 2. Be able to read and sing Chinese and Western musical scores; 3. Know the repair and maintenance of musical instruments; 4. Have a general knowledge of the names and evolution of ancient and modern musical instruments of our country.

(16) Architecture: 1. Know the essentials of architecture; 2. Be able to describe the differences, advantages, and disadvantages of Chinese and Western architecture; 3. Know the quality of water, wood, and metal materials; 4. Be able to draw a plan view, a three-dimensional view, and a detailed view of utensils; 5. Be able to create an architectural drawing and describe the construction method and materials used.

Shanghai Education Association's Tenth People's School Establishes a Public Advisory Office to Write Letters and Guide Accounts for the Public, and Resolve Difficulties in Daily Life

The Tenth People's School established by the Shanghai Education Association is located in the Daxing University School on Datong Road in Zhabei. In order to solve all the difficult problems of the uneducated public, the school has specially established a Public Advisory Office. The measures are recorded as follows: (1) This office is affiliated to the Tenth People's School of the Shanghai Education Association and is named the Public Advisory Office affiliated to the Tenth People's School; (2) The purpose of this office is to handle public inquiries and provide explanations and guidance; (3) The scope of work of this office is temporarily defined as follows: (A) Write notes, letters, invitations, couplets, and contracts entrusted by the public; (B) Explain textual difficulties; (C) Guide accounting methods; (D) Guide and solve difficulties encountered in daily life; (E) Guide matters needing attention in hygiene, home economics, and roads; (F) Guide legal and compliant procedures; (4) This office has a director, who is concurrently the director of teaching affairs of the People's School; (5) The working hours of this office are from 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM every day except holidays; (6) The services provided by this office are of an obligatory nature and no fees are charged. However, requests involving secrets, defamation of others, or violation of laws and customs may be refused; (7) The written documents handled by this office must be stamped with the office seal to show identification; (8) The paper used for writing entrusted documents shall be provided by the entrusting party; (9) These regulations are formulated in accordance with the methods for public advisory offices affiliated to schools promulgated by the Shanghai Education Bureau; (10) These regulations shall be submitted to the Shanghai Education Bureau for approval and implementation.

3rd Public Exhibition Cup International Handball Competition

丨First Round丨

November 28th, 29th, December 1st.

丨Second Round丨

December 5th, 6th, 7th.

Origin of the Public Exhibition Cup: This cup competition was initiated by the Shanghai YMCA, jointly organized by the Western YMCA, and donated by Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau. It is held twice a year, with the name of the winning team engraved on the cup, and the team holds it for a season. The competition is divided into singles and doubles, with ten groups in singles and five groups in doubles. The winner of each group is counted as one point. The competition adopts a three-round two-win system to determine the championship.

Results of the First Competition: The first competition was held last year on December 14th, 15th, 16th, 21st, 22nd, and 23rd. As a result, the Western team won. The results are as follows: (First Round) Western Team 10 points, Chinese Team 3 points; (Second Round) Western Team 7 points, Chinese Team 6 points.

Results of the Second Competition: The second competition was held this year on March 15th, 16th, 17th, 22nd, 23rd, and 25th. The results are as follows: (First Round) Western Team 9 points, Chinese Team 6 points; (Second Round) Western Team 8 points, Chinese Team 7 points. The championship was retained by the Western team.

About This Competition: This competition is scheduled to be held on November 28th, 29th, and December 1st (First Round) and December 5th, 6th, and 7th (Second Round). If necessary, the competition will still be held on December 12th, 13th, and 14th (Third Round). This year's Western team is still represented by the Western YMCA, while the Chinese team is represented by the Chinese YMCA. The Western team has been competing at the association recently. In addition to the original players, many players from McLens have been added, so the strength is quite strong. The Chinese team has been preparing for this competition for a long time. Due to the reconstruction of the Chinese YMCA's court and the holding of various competitions, as well as the enthusiasm and efforts of the players, there has been considerable progress in terms of skills, so there is great hope for this championship.

Chinese Walking Team Full Course Practice Tomorrow Veteran Zhou Yuyu Also Participates

In order to prepare for the 10,000-meter walk in the next World Games, the Chinese Walking Association has organized a preparatory committee and scheduled a three-year plan to focus on the work. Starting in September of this year, they first practiced ten miles, and this month they practiced seventeen miles. They started practicing last week, and the results were very good. Tomorrow (Sunday) at 7:30 AM, they will practice again. Those who join must gather on time at the intersection of Tongfu Road and Xieqiao Road and wait for departure. The route remains the same, and the end point is still at the intersection of Weihaiwei Road and Mahuo Road. Veteran Zhou Yuyu will accompany the walking. However, Zhou was accidentally injured in his left arm by a truck while serving as a referee during the public competition on the 12th. He has not fully recovered and has not been able to practice for two weeks. But he is still coming enthusiastically, which is commendable. Shi Jinsheng, who announced his retirement, had boils on his shoulders last time, and his arms could not swing. He has been neglecting his training for years. Now he is slightly better and intends to continue walking. It is said that he has joined the 50,000-meter practice, which will make the strength of our Chinese team even stronger. It is possible to join the 17-mile practice tomorrow.

Special Article: An Overview of Modern Chinese Educational Thought (7) - Narrated by Shu Xincheng, Recorded by Sun Yucai (5) The Period of Economic Revolution (Year 17 of the Republic, Year 22 of the Republic)

Our country's adoption of the new education system was originally forced by foreign aggression. Thirty years ago, the ruling authorities, due to repeated diplomatic defeats, eagerly sought to strengthen the country. They vigorously promoted new education based on the reasoning that "virtue is the strongest force, and the system of schools is most detailed in virtue. Japan's rise was the quickest, and the number of schools is the highest among Eastern countries." As for the advantages of the new education, its effectiveness, and the social environment and historical background it required, there was neither the time nor the ability to consider them at the time. Thus, this "new education system, unsuited to the local conditions, was implemented in a state of indiscriminate adoption for more than thirty years. Because it was too unsuited to the local conditions, the results produced in more than thirty years were far from what society had expected." The education system was therefore constantly changing, and educational thought rose and fell in over a dozen ways as described in the previous article. However, the sacred myth of education still existed in the minds of the general public, and governance-oriented education, urban education, and talent education still maintained their traditional advantages and stood firm. Before the 17th year of the Republic, the various facts of education's ineffectiveness were indeed clearly visible, but because the people of the country eagerly anticipated the success of the National Revolution, they believed that everything in the country could be gradually improved by its success, and education could also be effective with the reform of politics. Unexpectedly, the objective environment did not allow the realization of subjective expectations. In the five years since then, from the perspective of the entire China, although there has been some progress, the effectiveness of education is still the same as before, and even less than before in some places. The most obvious fact is that in terms of social effectiveness, production is declining daily, and in terms of school outcomes, graduates have even fewer opportunities. As a result, the function of education has become something that people doubt and investigate, and the sacred concept of education has gradually diminished and broken down with the facts. At the same time, due to the "September 18th Incident" of the 20th year of the Republic and the "January 28th Incident" of the 21st year of the Republic in Shanghai, educational thought underwent drastic changes and new developments. Now I will summarize it in four aspects.
