Essays

The Study of "Eating"

— Li Zhai

Almost all nationalities in the world have their own unique strengths. For example, the Germans excel in science and medicine; the Jews excel in accumulating wealth; the Japanese excel in rapidly imitating all advanced material civilizations; and the Americans excel in "innovating new styles." If someone were to ask: What is the unique strength of the Chinese nation? I would sit up straight and answer decisively: The most outstanding strength of the Chinese people in the world is "eating"! Populists or those who believe in "China First" will surely consider my statement as "self-abandonment"... "People must insult themselves before others insult them"! However, I have my own well-founded reply; please look at the facts!

"Eating" can be divided into two categories: one is direct and concrete "eating," and the other is indirect and abstract "eating." Our esteemed compatriots truly excel at both types of "eating," deserving to be called "masters of both"!

First, let's talk about concrete "eating." The Chinese will gather around a table with many "honored guests," slice open the skull of a live monkey, and everyone will scoop and eat the raw monkey brains. They will eat "Dragon Tiger Fight" and "Dragon Phoenix Grand Meeting," and they will eat shark fin soup that costs eighty yuan a bowl. If you and I could take a "vacation" from our family's "clothing, food, and housing" for three or four months, and book a table for three or five hundred yuan at a restaurant like Guanshengyuan or Xinya, at least half of the exotic dishes presented by those "Lingnan master chefs" would have names and contents that we wouldn't understand. All of these things considered, no matter how exquisite the Western cuisine at the Cathay Hotel is, selling for thirty or fifty yuan a dish, compared to the Chinese's "imaginative" "eating," Westerners are simply astonished and cannot even see our backs. However, these "eating" methods must be based on the premise of the "exploiting class." In another world at the "North and South Poles," there are also two-legged creatures like us who are eating corn buns, cornmeal, grass roots, tree bark, and Guanyin clay!

When it comes to abstract "eating," our "reference materials" are endless! In our "national opera," there are often lines like "eating the king's bounty, repaying the emperor's grace," and in history, there are often "great good old men" who "eat two thousand bushels of grain" or are "bestowed ten thousand households." From this, it can be seen that the ministers and generals of past dynasties all took abstract and indirect "eating" as their way of life.

In the past, scholars often called themselves or were described as "eating stipends." When they passed the imperial examinations, they became scholars, and were listed in the "top three," which was a consistent "eating" method for Chinese intellectuals who were divorced from the means of production: eating the Four Books and Five Classics, eating the eight-legged essay. This is the "eating" of the "Confucians."

Monks are famously "eating from all directions," but now there are many "highly knowledgeable" "senior monks" who have bank checks, villas, and mistresses, with round faces and bulging bellies. This is the "eating" of the "Buddhists": eating the Diamond Sutra, eating big and small dishes.

Zhang Tianshi carries the token and sword to the Great World to sell talismans, not hesitating to equate himself with "human meat," this is the "eating" of the "Taoists": eating spells.

"God" came to "visit the Celestial Empire" on the warships of the imperialists, so in addition to the Confucian, Buddhist, and Taoist realms, there was also a group of "eating the church." Since they "eat the church," wealth and beautiful women are all among them.

From the late Qing Dynasty to the present, many "great philanthropists" who managed dike construction and disaster relief funds have become wealthy and noble. This fact illustrates that some groups of "philanthropists" are "eating disasters," eating the lives and flesh of disaster victims.

According to reliable calculations, the total amount of donations to support the volunteer army against Japan was over 20 million yuan, but Ma Zhanshan and others received only 2 million yuan, with nine-tenths being swallowed up by "patriotic people." It can be seen that the way of life of these "patriots" is "eating the national crisis," which is eating the lives and blood of tens of millions of compatriots in Northeast China!

From "overthrowing the Manchus" to "anti-imperialist revolution," on the one hand, many revolutionary martyrs sacrificed their blood, and on the other hand, many "leaders" put villas, savings, and beautiful wives into their hands. After the "death" of a veteran who enjoyed a "national funeral" (actually a "provincial funeral"), a certain Zhou weekly magazine at Wanjing University wrote a eulogy: "Following the Premier for decades, lowering the flag for three days; accumulating family wealth of two million, with six concubines!" It can be seen how strong the "old revolutionary's" stomach was! This group of people can only be given the posthumous title: "eating the revolution" or "eating the blood of comrades"!

Others, such as good merchants, rely on "eating enemy goods" as a source of life. Also, some "editors," in the era of warlords, relied on writing parallel prose praising concubines to "eat" Zhang Zongchang, etc. When Zhang Zongchang went to Beppu, they also followed to Beppu. If Zhang Zongchang ate black dates, the Hanlin scholars could not follow him to the netherworld, but they would run to Shanghai to write a "preface" for someone's wife. It can be seen that the "eating" method of the "sacred door" is determined "according to the changes of the times."

There are too many "philosophers and patriots" who engage in the above "eating" methods, and the result is that China has become a mess. However, this phenomenon will certainly not be permanent. Once the lower classes, who eat corn buns, rough grains, grass roots, and tree bark, unite and engage in a historical general reckoning, then all those who engage in abstract "eating" may have a day when they "cannot eat it all and have to take it away"!

In the Broadcasting Studio

— Xiao Songjiang

It is said that friends who make a living by talking have been lucky this year, because the radio business has developed at a high speed within a year. If you have time to go to the balcony and look around, there are countless bamboo poles in the sky. At the same time, in every household, a group of people are eagerly trying out this new-fangled thing; however, radio has no rules. After playing for a while, there is always something going wrong. Nowadays, when everyone has free time, they listen to the radio.

No matter how you install the radio, you must have a square speaker to enjoy it. It is not a problem to get used to it. Although the broadcasting is only for one person, it is not a problem if everyone listens together. The requirements are just a few records and various musical scores.

Page 22

Actually, things seem easy, but once you start, you feel that every task requires experience. After spending months in the broadcasting studio without seeing the sun, I am writing a little to air out.

The most important responsibilities in the broadcasting studio are playing records and making announcements. Playing records is the easiest thing; the record player is electric, so you don't have to exert yourself to crank it. However, announcements are more troublesome. First, your voice must be steady, even, and clear. You have to keep your throat always at an even level, otherwise, it will affect the radio reception. For advertisements, naturally, someone will provide a script, but you must think of catchy phrases to make the listeners not feel annoyed every day. If you always introduce "This station is presenting," after reporting like this several times a day, you yourself would probably feel embarrassed.

Speaking of several red radio stations, they broadcast from nine or ten in the morning until one or two midnight every day, with no free time in the dozen or so programs. Listening to Suzhou storytelling and Shanghai灘 music is really tiring. You want to leave the broadcasting studio for a moment, but time is always controlling you, making your body feel like it is tied to a machine and you cannot be lazy.

Moreover, many guests visit the broadcasting studio (my words do not contain any hint of rejecting visitors). When broadcasting programs, you cannot greet them loudly, often offending them. I myself have been seen as an arrogant person, probably because I don't often entertain guests.

There is also a kind of suffering that listeners who close their eyes and relax on the sofa while listening to the radio can never imagine. It is already late autumn, and it is certainly comfortable to be warm in the broadcasting studio. However, when you go home after the program is over, you realize how bone-chilling the autumn night is. The most laughable thing is that on hot summer days, the windows of ordinary broadcasting studios are always closed to avoid external noise, even though they are there. Imagine a small broadcasting studio with velvet cloth around it, in the sweltering summer weather with no ventilation, the person shouting and singing is really like sitting next to a stove.

There are many interesting anecdotes and scandalous stories in the broadcasting studio. I would like to write them down when I have time for the readers of this publication to have a laugh.

Now the broadcasting time has arrived, please meet again next time in this publication.

Two Overseas Students

— Shi Ben

I didn't expect that in this suffocating and naive society of the eighteenth century, there would actually be two overseas students! This is such an honor! Not only their parents, clans, and relatives feel infinitely glorious, but also we townspeople, who share the same hometown, feel proud.

One of the two overseas students, surnamed Hu, came from an aristocratic family with both wealth and power. Spending eighteen thousand yuan to study abroad was not surprising. However, there was also one surnamed Zhu, whose family was ordinary, and his father was a hardworking farmer. He was not qualified to study abroad at all. Fortunately, Mr. Hu's father saw that he was intelligent and could be developed, so he subsidized him to accompany his son abroad, so that his son would not be lonely abroad. Therefore, this small town was able to produce two American students, one rich and one poor.

This spring, the two overseas students graduated from XX University in the United States and returned home after completing their studies.

When they returned home, it was like officials returning home in silk robes. Their parents were overjoyed, as if they had won 500,000 yuan in the lottery. Relatives and friends hosted banquets to welcome them, and the townspeople were stirred up by the title of "overseas student." Everyone ran to peek and catch a glimpse of their style, and kept saying, "Their parents are so glorious! Their sons have returned from studying abroad and can immediately become high officials. But, it's good for everyone when the neighbors become officials! Haha!" Because this semi-civilized town had never produced overseas students, and the townspeople's minds were often imprinted with the idea that returning from studying abroad was like passing the imperial examination in the Qing Dynasty, and they could immediately become high officials, they now worshiped and admired these two overseas students! It can be seen how glorious overseas students are in the countryside!

Before they had been back for a month, the townspeople were already spreading rumors: "Zhu XX has been invited by Jiang XX to be the XX Chief, and the National Government has sent a telegram to Hu XX, asking him to be the XX Minister." These ignorant townspeople all believed that overseas students were qualified to be XX Chiefs and XX officials, so such rumors arose unexpectedly!

However, the two of them were busy looking for a way out every day, asking friends and classmates for help. They were busy for three whole months without any hope. The townspeople couldn't believe that the overseas students had nothing to do.

The one surnamed Hu, because he was rich, had greater desires for seeking a job than the one surnamed Zhu. For example, when a relative introduced him to a position as a clerk in a foreign firm, he said, "Who wants to do this kind of slave job?" Another friend introduced him to a clerk position in the XX Municipal Government, and he also said, "Who wants to take on this kind of minor official position?". Unlike the one surnamed Zhu, he came from a poor background and had no good relatives or friends, so he could not get the clerk position that the one surnamed Hu did not want to do. After returning home for half a year, he was still unemployed. Once, there was an opportunity to be a primary school teacher, but he was afraid of losing the status of an overseas student because of the rumors spread by the townspeople, so he declined. Later, because of the pressure of life, out of frustration, he secretly went to Shanghai to work as a clerk under a foreigner, which was considered a solution to his overseas student's way out. When the one surnamed Hu heard about this, he was furious, thinking that this was insulting the personality of their overseas students and degrading the status of their overseas students. So, he chased after Zhu to Shanghai and rebuked him: "You useless thing, you don't care about the personality of us overseas students and come to do this shameful job of a clerk, willingly being a slave to foreigners. Think about it, I, who am much more noble than you, also refused to do the clerk position in a foreign firm because it was a slave job, and I also firmly declined the municipal government clerk position because I was afraid of losing the status of an overseas student... Now you are shamelessly doing this despicable job of a clerk, truly losing your personality and bankrupting your reputation, you are a disgrace to us overseas students..." Zhu was stunned by what he heard, unable to cry. Ashamed and resentful, he said in a trembling voice: "If I were as rich as you, and had no worries about life, I would also care about reputation and personality, but..." He was extremely sad and had no courage to continue speaking, so he could only cry. But, who will forgive his sorrow?

"Selling Oneself for Patronage"

— Li Yue

"Selling oneself" in the past feudal society was sometimes a thing that deserved people's sympathy and praise for a time. For example, selling oneself to bury one's father, mother, parents-in-law, or husband was said to be something that only filial sons and virtuous women with a spirit of self-sacrifice could do. This commendable thing was not only worthy of people's temporary sympathy and praise, but it was also something that would be remembered for generations to come, and would serve as an example for future generations. This means that "selling oneself" is not something that just anyone can do casually.

Things have changed in our current turbulent and chaotic society: Besides the filial sons and virtuous women who are determined to sacrifice themselves and can naturally do this "selling oneself" thing, other people of all kinds are equally courageous and determined to do this thing that ordinary people could not do before. Because this thing has a related relationship with "patronage" now, so many more people have already regarded this costless thing as the only "occupation" for making a living for life.

However, the "selling oneself for patronage" mentioned here can get a comfortable and enjoyable life without spending any money, and is clearly different from the business of prostitutes selling their smiles and screaming miserably in the cold wind on the streets during nights with rain and snow. Because when being a prostitute, although it is said that no capital is needed, you still have to take the money earned by letting people trample on your beauty and body to perm your hair, sell rouge and powder, cut fashionable clothes, wear flesh-colored silk stockings and high-heeled leather shoes, and also pay taxes and the rent for the second landlord, etc.: But the "selling oneself for patronage" mentioned here only needs to throw away all of your personality and soul completely, and single-mindedly follow the "master" like a "pug dog," running in and out and shouting left and right, and other than that, nothing else needs to be paid even slightly. Not only is beauty not needed, but the more ugly and fierce you are, the more you will get the "master's" favor and love, and there is a full hope that you will be promoted and become prominent and important, and you can "rely" on it.

However, "selling oneself" has the division of "whole sale" and "retail," so what you "rely" on is also proportionately different with "permanent" and "temporary." The permanent "rely" obtained by the so-called "whole sale" is that after swearing to follow the "master," you will always absolutely listen to the "master's" call, always absolutely take the "master's" will as your will, and absolutely cannot go to serve others, and no matter whether the "master" you "rely" on is a "Mount Tai" or an "iceberg," you must express loyalty and obedience, so that the "master" will allow it to "share blessings together." And the temporary "rely" obtained by "retail" is much more straightforward and free than "whole sale," but within the "sale" period, loyalty and obedience like a "pug dog" are undoubtedly still necessary conditions. For example, if the "master" gives it thirty yuan a day in "compensation," and tells it to harm the "master's" dissenting actions, then its task is only to be sure to promptly obey the order to complete it within the "sale" period, and the means of doing it can be up to it, and other than that, it can "damn everything else." But there is one thing that both "whole sale" and "retail" have in common, which is that in addition to "sharing blessings together" or "compensation," if you are unlucky enough to have to go to the execution ground to "be beheaded," then the "master" has no obligation to come forward to speak for you and ask for pardon, and the "sold out" "pug dog" should have no qualms, and absolutely go there with a happy and joyful expression. This means that those who throw away their personality, integrity, and soul to "sell themselves for patronage" and become "pug dogs" have no guarantee at all, although they can get a comfortable and enjoyable life without spending any money.

Opening your eyes and taking a look, a large group of promising young people are generally serving as "pug dogs" that are loyal and obedient to the "master"! I think: In our current turbulent and chaotic society, has being a "pug dog" become the only "way out" for making a living?…

"Not Afraid Even If I Die"

— Where to Go

People, you know; are originally this kind of clever thing, he knows what can be said can all be thought of, but what is thought of has some that cannot be said.

There are things that are said as soon as they are thought of. To say it politely, of course, it is candid; to say it impolitely, it is simply foolish. Because being a person requires being all things to all men, and speaking requires never revealing one's true intentions. For if not, people will see through this "mechanism in the sleeve," and once it is revealed, people will use this as a handle to attack you.

For example, talking about wanting a woman. If people ask if I want one, I will bite back and say no. By saying this, people will at least not be able to guess my true heart. Even if they want to laugh at me, they will not be able to laugh heartily. Furthermore, if I really want a woman, people will at least not be so wary of me, and I, in turn, can honestly guard against them. If things succeed, people can only stare in a daze; if not, I will also remain "unknown to gods or ghosts," and I only need to swallow the saliva in my throat quietly.

Talking about wanting to be an official is the same. Not telling the truth is always the best policy. When people ask, "Hey, there is a vacancy there, are you going to try for it?" When you hear this, it is best to put on a stern face and scold him "to the point of bloodshed, thoroughly and happily." Because putting on a stern face always makes people feel that it is genuine, let alone scolding with a stern face? In this way, you can both scold people and raise your own status. What is even cheaper is that you can make people go ahead with the matter without any suspicion. If it succeeds, "I will be my own high official, let them laugh and scold as they will," if not, it is worthwhile to scold people, vent your anger, and also grab a high-minded title.

Besides these, "understanding one thing leads to understanding all," naturally everything is the same. However, there are still some subtle minor problems in between. Of course, the more serious you are, the more people will trust you. However, if your "Kung Fu" is too shallow, you will inevitably reveal your true colors often. "The more you try to cover up, the more you reveal" is this kind of saying. Therefore, the general "old hands" are "experienced and profound" and "not flustered when facing the enemy." The more you "cut to the chase" and expose him nakedly, the more I will "insist on denying it" and "not change my original intention." It doesn't matter if my face turns red. The attitude must be firm, holding to the principle of "not being afraid even if I die." That is, even if people jump up and scold me, cry out that I am shameless, thick-skinned, and a hypocrite, I will still remain calm. In this way, "using softness to overcome hardness," the result is that people still have no way to deal with me.

Europeanization

— Guang Han

The minimum requirement is wearing a Western suit, and of course, shoes and hats must be uniform.

As for housing? A Western-style house is most suitable; otherwise, one should have a flush toilet and a Western-style washbasin and bathroom. At the very least, a sofa is indispensable.

Meals must be "grand": they cannot all be "grand," but if you have to eat "national dishes," it's okay. You can use knives and forks instead of chopsticks, which is not a departure from the principle of "Chinese essence, Western application." For snacks, it has to be bread and butter. To drink, either coffee or cocoa, as you please. Avoid using loose sugar; only use Taikoo sugar.

Walking: Shrug your shoulders, straighten your back, walk quickly, and dash around as if in an empty place. It would be even better to carry a "walking stick."

When walking with a woman, hold hands, and putting your arm around her waist is also acceptable.

Don't take cars too often; if not, then take first-class on the tram. Occasionally taking a rickshaw is also decent.

When you meet a friend, everyone should shake hands. (Nodding is still acceptable, but bowing is out of the question!)

Speaking is crucial. Being able to speak entirely in English or French, and hum a few Western songs, is top-notch. Next best is to insert a few Western words. Although there's no fixed rule for the amount, a ratio of ten to three is probably the most appropriate. If that's still too much, greet people with "Hello," say goodbye with "Au Revoir," call a gentleman "Mister," say "Sorry" for apologies, and you shouldn't have any trouble saying "Yes" and "No." This is the bare minimum. If you can't even do this, then you're not qualified to talk about Europeanization!

Envelopes should be Western-style. If you can't write foreign words,

you should still write the person's name and address horizontally, and the order must be reversed. The writing of names should be with the given name first and the family name last. Addresses, such as No. XX, XX Lane, XX Road, Shanghai, should be arranged as No. XX, XX Lane, XX Road, Shanghai. And don't forget to put the stamp in the upper right corner.

Printing your full name and address in one or two lines of foreign words on the back of your business card is indeed also very appropriate. It's both Europeanized and beautiful. It's also very convenient when interacting with foreigners.

Watching movies and dancing are "daily routines." Even those who are "nationalized" enjoy them, let alone those who are Europeanized?

Decorating your bookshelf with a few original Western books is also indispensable, regardless of whether you can understand them or not. It's best to carry a foreign newspaper when going out. Whether you can read it or not is not the issue, or perhaps you don't even intend to read it; just don't find it cumbersome. (As for knowing some current affairs, naturally, you are not forbidden from reading "national newspapers.")

Some people say that smoking is a bad habit, and "Lockhart" also tells us that nicotine contains toxic substances. But the gentlemen of the Analects Society quite encourage people to smoke, presumably because smoking won't cause much harm to one's character or endanger one's life. So, you might as well give it a try, because most foreigners like it. It's best to smoke cigars or hold a pipe, which is more generous.

If you can do these things, you can be considered fully Europeanized and have no regrets! If you're still not satisfied, then changing your hair is easy; with the help of chemicals, you can change its color. If you want blue eyes, a high nose, and white skin, then you'll have to consult doctors at beauty salons. If there's no way to do it, then it's beyond human power, not unwillingness; it should be understandable. Even genuine "foreign goods" wouldn't laugh at you for "drawing a tiger and failing to resemble it," right?

Novel

Shanghai (3)

— Zhang Lao San

(5) Dream

After being busy all day yesterday and not sleeping well at night, I sat on the sofa and felt a slight drowsiness. In a daze, it seemed like my younger brother and I were lying on the grass in front of our parents' graves. A gust of wind blew, and the graves burst open. Dad's eternally solemn face appeared before me from the grave. I let go of my younger brother's hand and wanted to run forward.

"Child, why did you leave your younger brother?"

A solemn voice.

"No."

"You've arrived in Shanghai?"

"Yes."

"Why?"

"To find the light I need?"

"You are surrounded by women!"

"I want revenge!"

"Good! Child, I am watching you at all times!"

The solemn face turned into a beautiful smile, and the grave disappeared without me knowing when. My younger brother was also gone. Everything was dark, only that beautiful smile, which暈 (I cannot translate this word with 100% accuracy, it seems to mean either blurred into an unbearable light or spread out) into a stinging radiance. It gradually approached me, finally making me unable to open my eyes.

"Dad, this is not the light I need."

I wanted to chase after my dad in the darkness but tripped over something.

"Brother, did you have a nightmare?"

Such a small voice came from the darkness.

(6) I am Sister Min

Opening my eyes, I was lying next to the sofa. The one speaking was the soulless woman I wanted to take revenge on. She was always smiling. I stood up and naturally put on Dad's solemn face.

"Why did you come into my room?"

A solemn voice.

"It's not a dream now!"

A playful tone.

"What?"

"Can't I come in?"

I didn't have Dad's experience and didn't know if it was okay to smile now, so I involuntarily revealed a trace of a smile. She was my enemy. I couldn't be surrounded by women. I wanted revenge. But that petite bourgeois woman was like a mischievous child. I wasn't afraid of the enemy's ferocity, I was afraid of the enemy's rubbery nature. When I lost the ability to deal with the enemy, I heard, "I am watching you at all times!" followed immediately by the second warning, "Don't let her go!" I suddenly grew courageous and restrained my smile.

"What do you mean?"

A solemn voice.

"Can you listen to my report?"

A playful tone.

"I am your mother's adopted daughter, I am Sister Min! Not the Sister Min you lost. We look very similar. For this reason, after your mother lost her beloved daughter, she adopted me. Sister Min was also the name your mother gave me, it was to commemorate her beloved daughter. At that time, I lived at the county high school, and we didn't have many opportunities to meet. A year later, my adopted mother passed away, and your father remarried, so I never went to your house again, because our relationship had been lost with the death of my adopted mother. I am an orphan living under my uncle's roof. After I stayed with your mother, she treated me like her own daughter, so I often went to her grave to cry bitterly. At the grave, every time I saw you leading your younger brother's hand coming from across the small bridge, I didn't want us to meet in such a setting: given our circumstances, it might evoke even greater grief."

That petite bourgeois woman was no longer a smiling, mischievous child, she was as solemn as a judge in a courtroom. She continued:

"Every time you came from across the small bridge, I would first escape from behind and hide among the desolate graves, secretly watching your actions. You always lay on the grass without saying a word, every day like that. Yesterday was of course the same, but, to some extent, I understood your unusual behavior. In yourself, perhaps you thought you were trying your best to stay calm. 'Go,' it was as if someone was urging me. I thought of this word. The night express train was the solution to our fate, younger brother, do you understand? That's how I came to Shanghai and ran into your room."

With a wry smile, the enemy I wanted to take revenge on was now a companion on the same journey.
